IN THE

COMPILED BY
GEORGE ARMSTRONG,
AND
REVISED BY
COLONEL SIR CHARLES W. WILSON,

PREFACE.

This Index has been compiled from the Old and New Testament and Apocrypha, the alterations in the Revised Version being noted in their places; from the ‘Memoirs and Name Lists of the Survey of Western Palestine;’ from that portion which is completed (as yet unpublished) of the ‘Memoirs and Name Lists of the Survey of Eastern Palestine;’ from Smith’s ‘Bible Dictionary;’ from the list drawn up by Sir George Grove for Clarke’s ‘Bible Atlas’ (S.P.C.K.); and from Conder’s ‘Handbook to the Bible’ and ‘Primer of Bible Geography,’ with numerous references to the ‘Quarterly Statements.’ The identifications adopted are those that will be found on the new maps (to be issued about the end of this year) of the Old and New Testament, covering both sides of the Jordan, and authorized by Colonel Sir Charles Wilson and Major Conder, R.E.

The Index to the Old Testament Sites includes upwards of 1,150 names of places in the Holy Land, Mesopotamia, Edom, the Desert of Sinai, and Egypt; being, it is believed, all those that are mentioned in the Old Testament and the Apocrypha.

The Index to the New Testament Sites contains 162 names, with references to Josephus (Whiston’s), in addition to those in the New Testament. Of these names 144 are known, 10 uncertain, and 8 not identified.

The identifications suggested by Major Conder as due to the Survey are marked with a star.

There are still 290 places mentioned in the Old Testament, in the East of Jordan, the Desert and Western Palestine, which remain to be identified. Reference is made in every case to the number of the sheet of the large and small maps on which the modern name will be found. Under the heading ‘Remarks,’ etc., will be found fuller particulars of the proposed site from the ‘Memoirs of Western Palestine.’

G. A.

1, Adam Street,
Adelphi,
March 22nd, 1888.

OLD TESTAMENT SITES

(Including all the Names to Sites in the Bible and Apocrypha.)

In the column ‘Modern Identification,’ those marked with a single ? are doubtful; those with double ?? are very doubtful; those marked with a star are due to the Survey. Abbreviations—‘R.V.’ is Revised Version; ‘A.V.’ is Authorized (Old) Version; ‘Mem.,’ with the letters, refers to the Memoirs of the Survey of Western Palestine; ‘Sh.’ is Sheet or Plan of the Large Map, with the number where the name is found; ‘B. R.,’ Robinson’s Biblical Researches.

Bible and Apocrypha Name. Refer­ences. Modern
Identifi­cation.		 No. of Sheet on ⅜-in. Map. Remarks, References, and No. of Sheet on Large Map.
ABANA, River
(R.V. ABANAH or AMANAH)		 2 Kings v. 12 Nahr Abanias, a branch of the Nahr Barada 3 and 4 One of the rivers of Damascus. Now called the Barada, rising in the Anti-Lebanon, near Zebdany, flowing through Suk Wady, Barada, receiving the waters of the copious spring of ʾAin Fijeh, and continuing its course through Damascus on to the great marsh on the plain called Bahret el Kibliyeh.
ABARIM, Mountains of Num. xxvii. 12; xxxiii. 47, 48; Deut. xxxii. 49 The range of Neba (Nebo) 15 Mountains beyond Jordan, the range of Nebo.
ABDON Josh. xxi. 30; 1 Chron. vi. 74 Kh. ʾAbdeh 6 A city of Ashar, 10 miles north of ʾAkka. (Mem. I. 170; Sh. III.)
ABEL, The Great Stone of 1 Sam. vi. 18 Deîr ʾAbân (?) near Beth-shemesh — Signifying ‘The great stone of the meadow’ (R.V.).—M. Clermont-Ganneau.
[p. 2] ABEL BETH-MAACHAH,
(R.V. ABEL BETH-MAACAH)		 2 Sam. xx. 14, 15, 18; 1 Kings xv. 20; 2 Kings xv. 29 Abl 6 Now a village, 6½ miles west of Banias, in Naphtali; also called Abel-maim. (Mem. I. 85 & 107; Sh. II.)
ABEL-CERAMIM,
(R.V. ABEL-CHERAMIM)		 Judg. xi. 33 Not identified — A place east of Jordan, beyond ‘Aroer.’
ABEL-MAIM 2 Chron. xvi. 4 Abl — Apparently identical with Abel Beth-maachah. (Compare with 1 Kings xv. 20.)
ABEL-MEHOLAH Judges vii. 22; 1 Sam. xviii. 19; 2 Sam. xxi. 8; 1 Kings iv. 12; xix. 16 ʾAin Helweh* 10 Jerome places it 10 miles south of Scythopolis, or at the present ‘ʾAin Helweh,’ 9½ miles south of Beth-shean. (Mem. II. 231; Sh. XII.)—Conder.
ABEL-MIZRAIM Gen. l. 11 Not identified — The threshing-floor of Atad. ‘Beyond Jordan.’ Placed by Jerome at Beth Hoglah, on the west bank.
ABEL-SHITTIM Num. xxxiii. 49 Kefrein, at northern margin of Ghôr es Seîsebân 14 Known in the days of Josephus as Abila; 60 stadia from the river. The town and palms have disappeared; but an extensive acacia-grove and some ruins still remain on the plain now called Seîsebân. (Conder’s Heth and Moab, p. 148.)
ABEZ,
(R.V. EBEZ)		 Josh. xix. 20 Kh. el Beida (?)* 6 A town of Issachar, named between Kishion and Remeth. Possibly the ruin el Beida = ‘white,’ at north limit of the plain of Esdraelon. (Mem. I. 309; Sh. V.)—Conder.
[p. 3] ABRONAH (Ebronah) Num. xxxiii. 34, 35 Not identified —
ACCAD Gen. x. 10 Nisibis (??) — One of the cities in the land of Shinar. Nisibis, a city on the Khabour river at the north-east part of Mesopotamia, and midway between Orfa and Nineveh, is generally believed to occupy the ancient site.
ACCARON 1 Macc. x. 89 — See Ekron.
ACCHO,
(R.V. ACCO)		 Judg. i. 31 ʾAkka 6 St. Jean d’Acre. The Ptolemais of the 1st Book of Maccabees. A seaport town. (Mem. I. 145, 153, 160; Sh. III.)
ACHOR, Valley of Josh. vii. 24, 26; xv. 7; Is. lxv. 10; Hos. ii. 15 Wâdy Kelt 14 Now Wâdy Kelt, the deep ravine south of Jericho. (Mem. III. 167; Sh. XVIII.)
ACHSHAPH Josh. xi. 1; xii. 20; xix. 25 Kefr Yasîf (?)* 6 The present village, ‘Kefr Yasîf,’ 6 miles north-east of ‘Accho.’—Conder. Named between Beten and Alammelech, a city in Asher. Kh. Iksâf (Sh. II., p. 119), and Haifa (Sh. V.), have also been proposed. (Mem. I. 169; Sh. III.)
ACHZIB (1) Josh. xv. 44; Micah i. 14 ʾAin Kezbeh (?)* 14 A city of Judah, named with ‘Keilah’ and ‘Mareshah.’—Conder. See Chezib.
[p. 4] ACHZIB (2) Josh. xix. 29; Judg. i. 31; v. 17 ez Zîb — The Ecdippa of Josephus. The present town, ‘Ez Zîb,’ 8½ miles north of ‘Akka’ in ‘Asher.’ (Mem. I. 155; Sh. III.)
ADADAH Josh. xv. 22 ʾAdʾadah 14 One of the cities in the south of Judah, named with ‘Dimonah’ and ‘Kedesh.’ Probably the present ruin Adâdah in the desert east of Beersheba.
ADAM Josh. iii. 16 ed Dâmieh (?) 10 ‘A city on the Jordan, beside Zarthan.’ The name is probably preserved in that of Tell Dâmieh, near the ford of ed Dâmieh. (Mem. II. 387; Sh. XV.)
ADAMAH Josh. xix. 36 ed Dâmieh* 6 One of the fenced cities of Naphtali. Now the ruin ‘ed Dâmieh,’ 5 miles west of Tiberias. (Mem. I. 365; Sh. VI.)
ADAMI,
(R.V. ADAM-NEKEB)		 Josh. xix. 33 Kh. Admah* 10 A place named as being on the border of Naphtali. The present ruin ‘Admah,’ 5 miles south-west of the Sea of Galilee. (Mem. II. 89; Sh. IX.)—Conder.
ADAR, or HAZAR ADDAR
(R.V. ADDAR)		 Josh. xv. 3; 1 Macc. vii. 40–45 Not identified — A place on the south boundary of Palestine. ‘Jebel Maderah,’ in the desert, is proposed for this site. (Quarterly Statement, p. 61, 1881.)
ADASA Kh. ʾAdaseh 14 According to Josephus (12 Ant. x. 5; 5 Wars xi. 5) was 30 stadia from Beth-horon. Now the present ruin ʾAdaseh, 8 miles south of Jufna. (Mem. III. 106; Sh. XVII.)
[p. 5] ADDAN, or ADDON Ezra ii. 59; Neh. vii. 61 Not identified — One of the places from which some of the Captivity returned to Judea, who could not show their pedigree.
ADIDA 1 Macc. xii. 38; xiii. 13 Hadîtheh 10 A town on an eminence (13 Ant. vi. 4) in the Shephelah. The present village Hadîtheh, close to Lydda on east. See Hadid. (Mem. II. 297; Sh. XIV.)
ADITHAIM Josh. xv. 36 Hadîtheh — A town in the territory of Judah. Somewhere in the Shephelah. Named between Gederah (Jedîreh) and Gederothaim, thought to be another name for Hadid, which see.
ADMAH Gen. x. 19; xiv. 2–8; Deut. xxix. 23; Hosea xi. 8 Not identified — One of the cities of the plain mentioned with ‘Zeboim.’ Possibly ‘Adam’ (Sheet X.), or ‘el Adeimeh’ (Sheet XIV.), in the region of the Ciccar. (Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 241, and Primer of Bible Geography, p. 38.)
ADORAIM 2 Chron. xi. 9 Dûra 14 A fortified city, built by Rehoboam—the ‘Adora’ of Josephus. Now the village of ‘Dura,’ 5 miles west of Hebron. (Mem. III. 301–304; Sh. XXI.)
ADORA (Adoraim) 1 Macc. xiii. 20 Dûra 14 The Dûra of Josephus = Adoraim.
[p. 6] ADULLAM Gen. xxxviii. 1, 12–20; Josh. xii. 15; xv. 35; 2 Chron. xi. 7; Neh. xi. 30; Micah i. 15; 2 Macc. xii. 38 ʾAîd el Mîyeh, or Kh. ʾAîd el Ma 14 A city of Judah in the low country. Eusebius places it 10 miles east of Eleuther­opolis (Beit Jibrin.) ‘Kh. ʾAid el Mâ’ is about 8 miles to the north-east. A discovery of M. Clermont-Ganneau, now generally recognised. (Mem. III. 311; Sh. XXI.)
ADULLAM, Cave of 1 Sam. xxii. 1; 2 Sam. xxiii. 13; 1 Chron. xi. 15 The cave near the ruins of ʾAîd el Mîyeh 14 David’s hiding place. The cave near the ruins of ʾAîd el Mâ.
ADUMMIM, ‘Going up to,’ or ‘of’ Josh. xv. 7; xviii. 17 Tʾalat ed Dumm* 14 On the road from Jerusalem to Jericho. (Mem. III. 172; Sh. XVIII.)—Mr. C. F. T. Drake.
AHAVA, River of
(A Place or a River)		 Ezra viii. 15, 21, 31 Hit (?) — Not identified with any certainty, but supposed to be the modern ‘Hit’ on the Euphrates, due east of Damascus. The Theras of Esd. viii. 41–61.
AHLAB Judg. i. 31 el Jish (?) 6 A city of Asher, from which the Canaanites were not driven out. Supposed to be the Giscala of Josephus and the Talmudic Gush Halab. The modern village, ‘el Jish,’ is thought to represent the ancient site; but ‘el Jish’ is in Naphtali, some 6 miles from the territory of Asher. (Mem. I. 225; Sh. IV.)

Aija, same as Ai (Neh. xi. 31)		 Gen. xii. 8; xiii. 3; Josh. vii. 2–5; viii. 1–29; ix. 3; x. 1, 2; xii. 9; Ezra ii. 28; Neh. vii. 32; Jer. xlix. 3 et Tell, or Kh. Haiyan* 14 Called by Josephus ʾAina; was ‘close to’ Bethel. The claims to this royal city lie between ‘et Tel,’ a mound 1⅜ miles to the E.S.E. of Bethel, and ‘Kh. Haiyan,’ near Deir Diwan, 2⅛ miles S.E. of Bethel. The former advocated by Col. Sir Charles Wilson and others, the latter by Capt. Conder (Mem. II. 372; III. 30; Sh. XVII.)

ARCHI Josh. xvi. 2; 2 Sam. xv. 32; xvi. 16; xvii. 5, 14; 1 Chron. xxvii. 33 ʾAin ʾArîk* 14 The present village ʾAin ʾArîk. (Mem. III. 7; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
ARDATH 2 Esd. ix. 26 Not identified — ‘The field called Ardath.’
ARGOB Deut. iii. 4, 13, 14; 1 Kings iv. 13 el Lejjah 8 A district of country in Bashan, in later times Trachonitis, now called el Lejjah.
 Dr. Porter says: ‘It is wholly composed of black basalt, which appears to have issued from innumerable pores in the earth in a liquid state, and to have flowed out on every side. Before cooling its surface was violently agitated, and it was afterwards shattered and rent by internal convulsions. The cuplike cavities [p. 15]from which the liquid mass was extruded are still seen, and likewise the wavy surface a thick liquid assumes which cools while flowing. The rock is filled with little pits and air-bubbles: it is hard as flint, and emits a sharp metallic sound when struck. This ungainly and forbidding region is thickly studded with deserted cities and villages, in all of which the dwellings are solidly built’ (p. 238).

Deut. iii. 17; iv. 49; Josh. x. 40; xii. 3; xiii. 20 ʾAyûn Mûsa, or The Slopes of Neba 15 In the old version is rendered ‘The springs of Pisgah,’ and has generally been identified with ‘ʾAyûn Mûsa,’ the famous springs under Mount Nebo. The Revised Version gives ‘the slopes of Pisgah.’ (Heth and Moab, p. 131.)
ASHER, Tribe of Josh. xix. 24–31; Josephus v. Ant. 1, 22 —
ASHER Josh. xvii. 7 Not identified — Named with Michmethah as being on the borders of Manasseh. According to Reland it is a double name Asherham-Michmethah. (Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 264, and Mem. II. 169; Sh. XI.)
ASHKELON, ASKELON Judg. i. 18; xiv. 19; 1 Sam. vi. 17; 2 Sam. i. 20; Jer. xxv. 20; xlvii. 5, 7; Am. i. 8; Zeph. ii. 4, 7; Zech. ix. 5 ʾAskalân 13 The present ruined city ʾAskalân, on the coast of Philistia. (Mem. III. 237; Sh. XIX.)
ASHKENAZ Jer. li. 27 One of the ‘Kingdoms of Ararat.’
[p. 18] ASHNAH (1) Josh. xv. 33 Kefr Hasan (?)* 14 ‘A city of Judah.’ The ruined town ‘ʾAslin,’ between ‘Zorah’ and Eshtaol, has been proposed for this site.
ASHNAH (2) Josh. xv. 43 Not identified — ‘A city of Judah.’ Idhnah, 5 miles south-east of Beit Jibrin, has been suggested.
ASHTAROTH Deut. i. 4; Josh. ix. 10; xii. 4; xiii. 12, 31; 1 Chron. vi. 71 Tell ʾAshtarah (?) 7 ‘A city in Bashan.’ Very probably Tell ʾAshtarah in Jaulan. (Across the Jordan, p. 209.)
ASHTEROTH KARNAIM Gen. xiv. 5; 1 Macc. v. 26, 43, 44; 2 Macc. xii. 21, 26 Tell ʾAshtarah (?) 7 The Samaritan version of the Pentateuch renders ‘Ashteroth Karnaim,’ by the name ‘Sunamein,’ a town on the Haj road, 28 miles south of Damascus. Tell ʾAshtarah farther north is also possible.
ASIA 2 Esdr. xv. 46; xvi. 1; 1 Macc. viii. 6; xi. 13; xii. 39; xiii. 32; 2 Macc. iii. 3; x. 24 Asia Minor — Asia is here used in its earlier sense, for Asia Minor or the country north of the Tarsus mountains.
ASPHAR, The Pool of 1 Macc. ix. 33; Ant. xiii. 1, 2 Not identified — In the wilderness of Tekoa.
ASSYRIA Very frequently mentioned —
ATAD, Threshing floor of Gen. l. 10, 11 Not identified ‘Beyond Jordan.’
ATARGATIS, Temple of 2 Macc. xii. 26 At Ashteroth Karnaim —
[p. 19] ATAROTH (1) Num. xxxii. 3, 34 Kh. ʾAttarûs (?) 15 In the land of Jazer and Gilead, built by Gad. Possibly the ruins of ʾAttarus, north of the river Arnon.
ATAROTH (2) Josh. xvi. 7 Not identified 10 Perhaps ‘Tell et Trûny,’ at the foot of the hills in the Jordan Valley. (Mem. II. 403; Sh. XV.; also p. 393, under the name Kh. Kaswah.)—Conder.
ATAROTH (3) Josh. xvi. 2 Same as Ataroth Adar —

(R.V. AZEL)		 Zech. xiv. 5 Not identified — The limit to which the valley or ravine of the Mount of Olives shall reach.

AZZAH
(R.V. GAZA)		 Deut. ii. 23; 1 Kings iv. 24; Jer. xxv. 20 Gaza — Identical with Gaza, which see. (In 1 Chr. vii. 28, the Revised Version reads Azzah, in the margin Ayyah.)
BAAL 1 Chron. iv. 33 Same as Baalath Beer — See Baalath Beer.
BAALAH Josh. xv. 9, 10; 2 Sam. vi. 2; 1 Chron. xiii. 6 Same as Kirjath Jearim — Another name for Kirjath-jearim or Kirjath-baal. (In 2 Sam. vi. 2, the Revised Version reads Baale Judah.)
BAALAH, BALAH or BILHAH Josh. xv. 29; xix. 3; 1 Chr. iv. 29 Not identified — A town in the south of Judah. (Mem. III. 261; Sh. XX.)
BAALAH, Mount Josh. xv. 11 Not identified — Named between ‘Ekron’ and ‘Jabneel.’ Probably one of the tops on the ridge running north of ‘el Mughâr’ (Makkedah).
BAALATH Josh. xix. 44; 1 Kings ix. 18; 2 Chron. viii. 6 Belʾaîn* 10 Perhaps the village Belʾaîn, and identical with the town in Kings ix. 18, Ant. viii. 6, 1. (Mem. II. 296; Sh. XIV.)—Conder.
BAALATH BEER Josh. xix. 8; 1 Sam. xxx. 27 Not identified — In the south part of Judah. Also called Ramah or Ramath of the South.
BAAL-GAD Josh. xi. 17; xii. 7; xiii. 5 Bâniâs (?) 7 ‘In the valley of Lebanon, under Mount Hermon.’ (Bâniâs, Schwarz & Robinson.) (Mem. I. 109; Sh. II.)
BAAL-HAMON Cant. viii. 11 Not identified — Perhaps Amana (Conder). See Balamo.

BAAL-HERMON, Mount Judg. iii. 3; 1 Chron. v. 23 Mount Hermon; Jebel esh Sheikh 3 Also called Mount Hermon, Deut. iii. 8; ‘Sirion,’ and ‘Shenir,’ Deut. iii. 9; Mount Zion, Deut. iv. 48. Now called Jebel esh Sheikh.
BAAL-MEON Num. xxxii. 38; 1 Chron. v. 8; Ezek. xxv. 9 Tell Mʾaîn 15 See Beth-baal-meon. A town of Reuben.
BAAL-PERAZIM 2 Sam. v. 20; 1 Chron. xiv. 11 Not identified — One of the scenes of David’s victories in the neighbourhood of the Valley of Rephaim.
BAAL-SHALISHA 2 Kings iv. 42 Kefr Thilth* (?) 10 Kh. Sirîsia is 14 miles north-east of Lydda. This place is identified in the Onomasticon with Baal Shalisha. The village Kh. Kefr. Thilth is 4 miles further on. (Mem. II. 299; Sh. XIV.) See Conder’s Bible Handbook, p. 404.
BAAL-TAMAR Judg. xx. 33 ʾAttâra (?) 14 Jewish tradition identifies the site with the large ruin ʾAttâra, near Gibeah of Benjamin.
BAAL-ZEPHON Ex. xiv. 2, 9; Num. xxxiii. 7 Not identified — A place in Egypt near which the Israelites crossed the Red Sea.
BABEL, Tower of Gen. x. 10; xi. 4, 5, 9 Birs Nimrûd —
[p. 23] BABYLON Very frequently mentioned — On the Euphrates. Usually connected with Birs Nimrûd.
BACA, Valley of Ps. lxxxiv. 6 Not identified — Signifying Valley of Weeping, or Balsam trees. (R.V.)
BAHURIM 2 Sam. iii. 16; xvi. 5; xvii. 18; xix. 16; 1 Kings ii. 8 Kh. ʾAlmît (??) 14 The Targum of Jonathan reads Almon (ʾAlmît). Identical with Alemeth and Almon, which see.

(R.V. BAYITH)		 Isaiah xv. 2 Not identified — In Moab.

BAMOTH, in the Valley
(R.V. to the Valley)		 Num. xxi. 20 ‘High places’ or ‘altars’ 15 This would perhaps refer to the dolmens in Wâdy Jedeid, immediately north of ‘el Maslûbîyeh.’ (See Heth and Moab, p. 144.)
BASCAMA 1 Macc. xiii. 23 Not identified — A place in Gilead. The scene of Jonathan the Hasmonean’s death.
BASHAN Num. xxi. 33; xxxii. 33; Deut. i. 4; iii. 1, 14; iv. 43; xxix. 7; xxxii. 14; xxxiii. 22; Josh. ix. 10; xii. 4; xiii. 11, 12, 30; xvii. 1, 5; xx. 8; xxi. 6, 27; xxii. 7; 1 Kings iv. 13–19; 2 Kings x. 33; 1 Chron. v. 11, 16, 23; vi. 62; Neh. ix. 22; Ps. xxii. 12; lxviii. 15, 22; cxxxv. 11; cxxxvi. 20; Isa. ii. 13; xxxiii. 9; Jer. xxii. 20; l. 19; Ezek. xxvii. 6; xxxix. 18; Am. iv. 1; Micah vii. 14; Nah. i. 4; Zech. xi. 2 6, 7, 11, 12 A district on the east of Galilee, extending from the borders of Gilead on the south to Mount Hermon on the north, and from the Jordan Valley on the west, to [p. 24]Bozrah on the east. The later Aramaic name, Batanea, applied to the south part of the district. It perhaps survives in the modern district name, el Butein, south-east of Galilee and in Ard el Bathania, further east. (See Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 315.)

BEER-ELIM Isa. xv. 8 Not identified — On the border of Moab.
BEER-LAHAI-ROI Gen. xvi. 14; xxiv. 62; xxv. 11 ʾAin Muweileh (?) 20 Between ‘Kedesh’ and Bered, in the south of Judah. The well ‘ʾAin Muweileh,’ 12 miles to the west of ‘ʾAin Kadîs,’ is supposed by Rowlands to be the ancient one.
BEEROTH Deut. x. 6 Not identified — One of the camping-stations of the Israelites. ‘Beerothe Bene-Jaakan’ = the wells of the children of Jaakan.
BEEROTH Josh. ix. 17; xviii. 25; 2 Sam. iv. 2, 3, 5, 9; xxiii. 37; Ezra ii. 25; Neh. vii. 29; 1 Chron. xi. 39 Bîreh 14 ‘A city of Benjamin.’ The present village ‘Bîreh,’ a day’s journey from Jerusalem, on the main road to Shechem and the north. (Mem. III. 88; Sh. XVII.)
BEER-SHEBA Gen. xxi. 14–31; 33; xxii. 19; xxvi. 23, 33; xxviii. 10; xlvi. 1, 5; Josh. xv. 28; xix. 2; Jud. xx. 1; 1 Sam. iii. 20; viii. 2; 2 Sam. iii. 10; xvii. 11; xxiv. 2, 7, 15; 1 Kings iv. 25; xix. 3; 2 Kings xii. 1; xxiii. 8; 1 Chron. iv. 28; xxi. 2; 2 Chron. xix. 4; xxiv. 1; xxx. 5; Neh. xi. 27, 30; Am. v. 5; viii. 14 Bîr es Sebʾa 13 The present ruin ‘Bîr es Sebʾa,’ with three wells. (Mem. III. 394; Sh. XXIV.)
[p. 26] BEESH-TERAH Josh. xxi. 27 Same as Ashtaroth — In the Hauran, another name for Ashtaroth, which see. Considered by Gesenius as a contracted form of Beth-Ashtaroth.

BETH-PAZZEZ Josh. xix. 21 Not identified — Mentioned with En-gannim and En-haddah of Issachar.
[p. 34] BETH-PEOR Deut. iii. 29; iv. 46; xxxiv. 6; Josh. xiii. 20 Mareighât (?)* 14 (Conder’s Heth and Moab, p. 14, and Quarterly Statement, 1882, p. 88.) See Peor (Num. xxii. 28), which is perhaps Minyeh, at west end of same ridge.
BETH-REHOB (1) Judg. xviii. 28 Hunîn (?) — Somewhere near the town of Laish or Dan. Possibly Hunîn, a fortress commanding the plain of Hûleh, in which the city of Dan (Tell el Kâdy) lay. (Robinson.)
BETH-REHOB (2) 2 Sam. x. 6 Not identified — An Aramean state south of Zobah and near the Euphrates.
BETHSAMOS 1 Esdr. v. 18 Hizmeh — Same as Beth Azmaveth and Azmaveth, which see.
BETH-SAN 1 Macc. v. 52; xii. 40, 41 — See Beth-shean.
BETH-SHEAN or BETH-SHAN Josh. xvii. 11, 16; Judg. i. 27; 1 Sam. xxxi. 10, 12; 2 Sam. xxi. 12; 1 Kings iv. 12; 1 Chron. vii. 29 Beisân 10 Represented by the modern town ‘Beisân’ and the extensive ruins surrounding it. (Mem. I. 101–107; Sh. IX.)
BETH-SHEMESH (1) Josh. xv. 10; xxi. 16; 1 Sam. vi. 9, 20; 1 Kings iv. 9; 2 Kings xiv. 11; 1 Chron. vi. 59; 2 Chron. xxv. 21; xxviii. 18 ʾAin Shems 14 On the boundary of Judah; now the ruins called ‘ʾAin Shems’ in the valley of Sorek. (Mem. III. 35, 60; Sh. XVII.)
[p. 35] BETH-SHEMESH (2) Josh. xix. 22 ʾAin es Shemsîyeh (??)* 10 A city of Issachar. Possibly ʾAin esh Shemsîyeh, in the Jordan Valley, south of Beisân. (Mem. II. 231; Sh. XII.)—Conder.
BETH-SHEMESH (3) Jer. xliii. 13 Heliopolis — In the Middle Ages Heliopolis was called Ain Shems, by the Arabs. A ruin 10 miles north-east of Cairo. (Robinson, i. 25.)
BETH-SHEMESH (4) Josh. xix. 38; Judg. i. 33 Kh. Shemsîn (?)*
Kh. Shemʾa (??)		 6 Thought by some to be Kh. Shemʾa, 3 miles west of Safed. One of the ‘fenced cities’ of Naphtali. (Mem. I. 246; Sh. IV.) Possibly Kh. Shemsîn, east of Mount Tabor.—Conder, Sh. VI.
BETH-SHITTAH Judg. vii. 22 Shutta (?) 10 Was in or near Jordan Valley. The name exists at Shutta (Sheet IX.), where Robinson places this site.
BETHSURA 1 Macc. iv. 29, 61; vi. 7, 26, 31, 49, 50; ix. 52; x. 14; xi. 65; xiv. 7, 33; 2 Macc. xi. 5; xiii. 19, 22 Beit Sûr — The Beth-zur of Joshua xv. 58, etc.
BETH-TAPPUAH Josh. xv. 53 Tŭffûh 14 Now represented by the modern village Tŭffûh, west of Hebron. (Mem. III. 310, 379; Sh. XXI.)
[p. 36] BETHUL or BETHUEL Josh. xix. 4; 1 Chron. iv. 30 Not identified 14 Possibly the small village ‘Beit Aûla,’ 5 miles west of Hûlhûl. Mentioned with ‘Eltolad’ and ‘Hormah,’ and belonging to Simeon. (Mem. III. 302; Sh. XXI.)
BETHULIA Judith iv. 6; vi. 10, 11, 14; vii. 1–20; viii. 3, 11; x. 6; xi. 9; xii. 7; xiii. 10; xv. 3, 6; xvi. 21, 23 Melithia (?)* 10 The village Methilieh, 5 miles south of Jenin. (Mem. II. 156; Sh. XI.)—Conder.
In the Middle Ages the name of Bethulia was given to the ‘Frank mountain’ south of Jerusalem (Rob., i. 479), later to ‘Safed,’ in Upper Galilee (Rob., ii. 425). ‘Sanur,’ immediately south of Methilieh, has been proposed; but the site of Methilieh appears to meet all the requirements. (Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 289.)
BETH-ZACHARIAS See Bath Zacharias —
BETH-ZUR Josh. xv. 58; 1 Chron. ii. 45; 2 Chron. xi. 7; Neh. iii. 16 Beit Sûr 14 Between Hŭlhûl and Gedor in the mountains of Judah. The present ruined town, Beit Sûr, 4 miles north of Hebron. (Mem. III. 311; Sh. XXI.)
BETOLIUS 1 Esdr. v. 21 Bethel — = Bethel.
BETO­MESTHAM Judith iv. 6; xv. 4 Kh. Massîn(??)* 10 A town ‘over against Esdraelon, facing the plain that is near Dothaim.’ Possibly Kh. Massîn, 8 miles south-west of Tell Dothan.
[p. 37] BETONIM Josh. xiii. 26 Not identified — ‘A town in Gad.’ The name ‘Bataneh’ applies to a heap of ruins, 3½ miles to south-west of es Salt.
BEZEK (1) Judg. i. 4, 5 Bezkah (??)* 14 In Judah. Perhaps the present ruin, Bezkah, 6 miles south-east of Lydda. (Mem. III. 36; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
BEZEK (2) 1 Sam. xi. 8 Kh. Ibzîk* 10 Now Kh. Ibzîk, 13 miles north-east of Shechem. (Mem. II. 231, 237; Sh. XII.)—Conder.
BEZER, IN THE Wilderness Deut. iv. 43; Josh. xx. 8; xxi. 36; 1 Chr. vi. 78 Kŭsr el Besheir (?) 14 A town of Reuben ‘in the wilderness’ upon ‘the plain’ or table-land. One of the six cities of refuge. The name ‘Kŭsr el Besheir’ occurs near Dibon, and was proposed by the late Professor Palmer.
BEZETH 1 Macc. vii. 19 Mt. of Olives (?), or Bezetha (?) — Possibly Bezetha, at Jerusalem. (Mem. III. 312; Sh. XXI.)
BILEAM 1 Chron. vi. 70 In the Wâdy Belʾameh.* Not identified 10 A town in western Manasseh. In Joshua xvii. 11, Ibleam. In Joshua xxi. 25, Gath-rimmon. The name is still recognisable in Wâdy Belʾameh, near Jenîn. (Mem. II. 47–48; Sh. VIII.)
BILHAH 1 Chron. iv. 29 Not identified — A town of Simeon; also called Baalah and Balah.
[p. 38] BITHRON 2 Sam. ii. 29 Not identified — A district on the east side of the Jordan Valley, and between the Jordan and Mahanaim.
BIZJOTHJAH
(R.V.
BIZI­OTHIAH)		 Josh. xv. 28 Not identified — A town in the south of Judah, named next to Beer-sheba.
BOCHIM Judg. ii. 1, 5 Not identified — A place on the west of Jordan above Gilgal, so called because the people ‘wept’ there.
BOHAN, Stone of Josh. xv. 6; xviii. 17 Not identified 14 A landmark on the boundary between Benjamin and Judah. Placed at ‘Hajr el Asbâh,’ on the cliff to the west of the north end of the Dead Sea (Ganneau)—uncertain. (Mem. III. 199; Sh. XVIII.)
BOSOR 1 Macc. v. 26 Busr el Hariri (?) 7 A fortified city on the east of Jordan. Named with the cities of Bosora, Alemais, etc., etc. Probably Busr el Hariri, 5 miles south-east of Edrei.
BOSORA 1 Macc. v. 26, 28 Busrah 12 A fortified city on the east of Jordan, mentioned with ‘Bosor,’ etc. Probably ‘Bozrah,’ east of Bashan.
BOZEZ 1 Sam. xiv. 4, 5 The north cliff of Wâdy Suweinît 14 The north cliff of the valley of ‘Michmash,’ and nearly opposite is the rugged precipice of ‘Seneh.’ (See Conder’s Tent Work in Palestine.)
[p. 39] BOZKATH or BOSCATH Josh. xv. 39; 2 Kings xxii. 1 Not identified — A city of Judah, mentioned between ‘Lachish’ and ‘Eglon.’
BOZRAH OF EDOM (1) Gen. xxxvi. 33; 1 Chron. i. 44; Isa. xxxiv. 6; lxiii. 1; Jer. xlix. 13, 22; Amos i. 12; Micah ii. 12 el Buseirah 21 Now the ruins called ‘el Buseirah,’ in Edom, south-east of the Dead Sea. (Burckhardt, 407; Robinson, ii. 167.)
BOZRAH OF MOAB (2) Jer. xlviii. 24 Probably same as Bezer, in the wilderness, which see. 12 Is perhaps the Bosor of Moabite Stone in Moab, but see preceding.
CABBON Josh. xv. 40 Not identified — A town in the low country of Judah.
CABUL Josh. xix. 27; 1 Kings ix. 13 Kâbûl 6 The present village, ‘Kabûl,’ 9 miles east of ʾAkka. Named as one of the places on the boundary of Asher. (Robinson, iii. 87–8; Mem. I. 308; Sh. V.)

(R.V. KAIN)		 Josh. xv. 57 Kh. Yukîn 14 Named between Zanoah and Gibeah. Possibly the ruin Yukîn, 3 miles south-east of Hebron. (Mem. III. 312; Sh. XXI.)

CAMON
(R.V. KAMON)		 Judg. x. 5 Not identified — A city of Gilead, and the place where Jair, one of the Judges of Israel, was buried. v. Ant. 7, 6.
CANAAN, The Land of Gen. xii. 5; xxiii. 2, 19; xxxi. 18; xxxiii. 18; xxxv. 6; xxxvii. 1; xlviii. 3, 7; xlix. 30; Num. xiii. 2, 17; xxxiii. 40, 51; Josh. xxi. 2; Judg. xxi. 12; etc., etc. Western Palestine — The low country of the Jordan Valley and the Mediterranean coast. The word means ‘Lowlands.’ It is sometimes applied to all Palestine.
CAPHAR-SALAMA 1 Macc. vii. 31; xii. Ant. 10, 4 Not identified — Kefr Silwan (Smith’s Bible Dictionary), near Jerusalem. The village Selmeh, near Joppa. (Conder, Handbook to the Bible.)

[p. 42] CHALDEA or CHALDAEA Jer. l. 10; li. 24, 35; Ezek. xi. 24; xvi. 29; xxiii. 15, 16; Judith v. 6 — The most southern part of Babylonia. The name Kaldai occurs in cuneiform for an early tribe.
CHARACA 2 Macc. xii. 17 Not identified — East of Jordan, in Gilead—750 stadia from the city Caspis; position of Caspis not known.
CHARASHIM, Valley of
(R.V. GE-HARASHIM)		 1 Chron. iv. 14; Neh. xi. 35 Kh. Hirsha (?)* 9 Near Lod and Ono (Neh. xi. 35). The name is preserved in the ruin Hirsha, 4½ miles to the east of Yalo (Sh. XVII.), and 12½ south-east of Lydda. The Wâdy from it passing Yâlô and joining Wâdy Selmân (the Valley of Ajalon) is one of the principal watercourses leading by Lod and Ono. (Mem. III. 36; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.

(R.V. CHEPHAR-AMMONI)		 Josh. xviii. 24 Kh. Kefr ʾÂna (?) 10 Mentioned among the towns of Benjamin. Thought to be the ruin ‘Kefr ʾÂna,’ 3 miles north of Bethel. (Mem. II. 299; Sh. XIV.)
CHEPHIRAH Josh. ix. 17; xviii. 26; Ezra ii. 25; Neh. vii. 29 Kefîreh 14 The ruin Kefîreh, 8 miles north-west of Jerusalem. 1 Esdr. v. 19, Caphira. (Mem. III. 36; Sh. XVII.)
[p. 43] CHERITH,
The Brook		 1 Kings xvii. 3, 5 Not identified — Jerome (Onomasticon Chorath) would place the Cherith beyond Jordan. Schwarz, ‘Wâdy Alias or Yabis,’ opposite ‘Beth Shean.’ Marino Sanuto, in 1321, makes it run by Phasaelis,—Herod’s city in the Jordan Valley. Robinson proposed ‘Wâdy Kelt,’ behind Jericho. The expression ‘facing’ Jordan favours the view that it was east of that river.
CHERUB Ezra ii. 59; Neh. vii. 61 Not identified 14 Possibly in Babylonia, but uncertain. One of the (five) places from which some of the Captivity returned and could not prove their pedigree.
CHESALON Josh. xv. 10 Kesla 14 On Mount Jearim. The name is preserved in Kesla, the village 10 miles west of Jerusalem. (Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 259; Mem. III. 25, 26; Sh. XVII.)
CHESIL Josh. xv. 30 Not identified Same as Bethul 14 In Josh. xix. 4, Bethul. 1 Chr. iv. 30, Bethuel.
CHESULLOTH Josh. xix. 18 Iksâl 6 The present village, Iksâl of Issachar. The Xaloth of Josephus, or Chisloth Tabor. (Mem. I. 365; Sh. VI.)
CHETTIIM 1 Macc. i. 1 Chittim or Macedonia —
[p. 44] CHEZIB Gen. xxxviii. 5 ʾAin Kezbeh (?)* 14 The name appears to linger in that of ʾAin Kezbeh. Possibly Beit Nettîf near it. (Mem. III. 36; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
CHIDON, The Threshing-Floor 1 Chron. xiii. 9 Not identified — = Nachon, 2 Sam. vi. 6. Somewhere between Kirjath-jearim and Jerusalem.
CHILMAD Ezek. xxvii. 23 Kalwâdha — Near Baghdad. Named with ‘Sheba’ and ‘Asshur.’

Sea of		 Num. xxxiv. 11; Deut. iii. 17; Josh. xii. 3; xiii. 27 Sea of Galilee 6 Sea of Galilee or Bahr Tubarîya. By Josephus and Maccabees. Gennesar, which see.

CHITTIM Num. xxiv. 24; Isa. xxiii. 1, 12; Jer. ii. 10; Ezek. xxvii. 6; Dan. xi. 30 Cyprus — A Japhetic people or place, remote from Palestine, separated therefrom by sea. In Macc. i. 1, Chettims; 1 Macc. viii. 5, Citims; Gen. x. 4, 1 Chron. i. 7, Kittim. In Old Testament no doubt Cyprus is intended; but in Apocrypha, perhaps Macedonia. See Cyprus (Grove’s Bible Atlas).

COLA Judith xv. 4 Kh. Kâʾaûn (?)* 10 A place named with Chobai (Judg. xv. 4). Perhaps Kh. Kâʾaûn in the Jordan Valley. (Mem. II. 238; Sh. XII.)—Conder.
COS 1 Macc. xv. 23 Stanchio — Now called Stanchio or Stanko, an island in the Grecian Archipelago. For a good account of the island, see Clarke’s Travels, vol. ii., pp. 196–213, and 321–333.
CRETE 1 Macc. x. 67 The island of Crete.
CUSH Gen. x. 6, 8; 1 Chron. i. 8–10; Isa. xi. 11 See Ethiopia.
CYAMON Judith vii. 3 Tell Keimûn 10 ‘Lying in the plain over Esdraelom.’ Eusebius and Jerome identify it with Camon in Upper Galilee, the burial-place of Jair; see Camon. Now generally believed to be represented by Tell Keimûn (Jokneam), on the edge of the plain of Esdraelon, near the south-east corner of Carmel.
[p. 47] CYPRUS 1 Macc. xv. 23; 2 Macc. x. 13; xii. 2 Cyprus — The well-known island off the coast of Syria. In the Old Testament called Chittim and Kittim. (Grove’s Bible Index.) See Chittim.
CYRENE 1 Macc. xv. 23 el Krenna — A city of Africa, between Carthage and Egypt.

DINHABAH Gen. xxxvi. 32; 1 Chron. i. 43 Not identified — City of Bela, King of Edom.
DIZAHAB
(R.V. DI-ZAHAB)		 Deut. i. 1 Dahab (??) — Identified by Robinson (i. 147, ii. 187) with Dahab, a promontory on the western shore of the Gulf of Akabah.
DOCUS 1 Macc. xvi. 15 Near ʾAin Dûk 14 A fort somewhere near Jericho—the name is recoverable in ‘ʾAin Dûk.’ (Mem. III. 173; Sh. XVIII.)
DOPHKAH Num. xxxiii. 12, 13 Not identified — One of the camping stations of the Israelites, between Rephidim and the Sea.
[p. 52] DOR (DORA 1 Macc. xv. 11, 13, 25) Josh. xi. 2; xii. 23; xvii. 11; Judg. i. 27; 1 Kings iv. 11; 1 Chr. vii. 29 Tantûra 9 Jerome places it 9 miles (the exact distance is 8 miles) from Cæsarea, on the road to Ptolemais. The ruins of a city here exist near the modern village Tantûra. (Mem. II. 7; Sh. VII.)
DOTHAIM Judith iv. 6; vii. 3, 18; viii. 3 Tell Dôthân 10 = Dôthân, which see.
DOTHAN Gen. xxxvii. 17; 2 Kings vi. 13 Tell Dôthân 10 The present ruins and well, ‘Tell Dôthân,’ north of Samaria. (Mem. II. 215; Sh. XI. See also Vol. I. p. 368, under ‘Khan Jubb Yûsef.’)
DRAGON’S WELL Neh. ii. 13 Not identified — In the neighbourhood of Jerusalem.
DUMAH Josh. xv. 52 ed Dômeh 14 The present ruin, Dômeh, 10 miles south-west of Hebron. (Mem. III. 313; Sh. XXI.)
DURA, The Plain of Dan. iii. 1 Dûair (?) — The mound and vicinity of Dûair, south-east of Babylon.—M. Oppert.
EBAL, Mount Deut. xi. 29; xxvii. 4, 13; Josh. viii. 30, 33 Jebel Eslâmîyeh
Jebel et Tôr		 10 Now called Jebel Eslamîyeh, and Jebel et Tôr. (Mem. II. 186; Sh. XI.) Ebal, Gerizim, Olivet, and Tabor are all named Tôr or ‘summit.’
EBEN-EZER 1 Sam. iv. 1; v. 1; vii. 12; 6 Ant. ii. 2 Deir Abân (?)* 14 Jerome places near ‘Beth-shemesh,’ probably intending the site of the present village, Deir Abân, east of ʾAin Shems. See Shen. (Mem. III. 24; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
[p. 53] EBRONAH
(R.V. ABRONAH)		 Num. xxxiii. 34 Not identified — One of the camping stations of the Israelites.
ECBATANA Ezra vi. 2; Esdr. vi. 23; Jud. i. 1, 2, 14; Tob. iii. 7; vi. 5; vii. 1; xiv. 12, 14; 2 Macc. ix. 3 Takht-i-Suleiman and Hamadan — There were two places of this name. One the capital of Northern Media, now called Takht-i-Suleiman. The southern one the metropolis of the province of Media Magna (2 Macc. ix. 3), now Hamadan in Persia.—Smith’s Bible Dictionary.
ED, Altar of Josh. xxii. 34 Not identified — Somewhere east of Jordan.
EDAR, Tower of
(R.V. EDER, Tower of)		 Gen. xxxv. 21 Not identified 14 Jerome places it 1,000 paces from Bethlehem. (Mem. III. 28; Sh. XVII.)
EDER Josh. xv. 21 Not identified — One of the uttermost cities of Judah, towards the coast of Edom. Kh. el ʾAdâr, 5 miles south of Gaza, has been suggested (Henderson’s Handbook); but the situation is too far west apparently.
EDOM, IDUMEA, The Land of Mt. Seir Gen. xxv. 30; xxxii. 3; xxxvi. 1, 8, 9–43; Ex. xv. 15; Num. xx. 14; xxi. 4; xxiv. 18; Jos. xv. 1; Judg. v. 4; xi. 17, 18; 1 Sam. xiv. 47; 2 Sam. viii. 14; 1 Kings ix. 26; 2 Kings iii. 8, 20;[p. 54] viii. 20; xix. 7; 2 Chr. viii. 17; xxi. 8; xxv. 19; Ps. lxxxiii. 6; cviii. 9; Isa. xi. 14; xxxiv. 5; lxiii. 1; Jer. ix. 26; xxv. 21; xxvii. 3; xl. 11; xlix. 7, 17; Lam. iv. 21; Ezek. xxv. 12; xxxii. 29; xxxv. 15; xxxvi. 5; Dan. xi. 41; Joel iii. 19; Am. i. 6; ii. 1; ix. 12; Obad. i. 8; Mal. i. 4; etc. The district east of the Wâdy ʾArabah. See Mount Seir.
EDREI Num. xxi. 33; Deut. i. 4; iii. 1, 10; Josh. xii. 4; xiii. 12, 31 Ed Deraʾah 7 South-east of el Mezeirib.
EDREI (2) Josh. xix. 37 Yʾater (?)* 6 Probably the present village Yʾater, 11 miles south-east of Tyre. Allotted to Naphtali. (Mem. I. 205; Sh. IV.)—Conder.
EGLAIM Isa. xv. 8 Not identified — Thought to be identical with En-eglaim, which see.
EGLON Josh. x. 3, 5, 23, 34, 36, 37; xii. 12; xv. 39 Kh. ʾAjlân 13 The present mound and ruins, ʾAjlân, 16 miles north-east of Gaza. (Mem. III. 278; Sh. XX.)
EGYPT Very frequently mentioned
[p. 55] EKREBEL Judith vii. 18 ʾAkrabeh 10 The present village ʾAkrabeh, south-east of Nablus. (Mem. II. 389; Sh. XV.)—Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, 290.
EKRON (ACCARON, 1 Macc. x. 89) Josh. xiii. 3; xv. 11, 45, 46; xix. 43; Judg. i. 18; 1 Sam. v. 10; vi. 16; vii. 14; xvii. 52; 2 Kings i. 1, 2–16; Jer. xxv. 20; Am. i. 8; Zeph. ii. 4; Zech. ix. 5, 7 ʾAkir 13 Now the village ʾAkir, in Philistia, 6 miles west of Gezer. The Accaron of the Crusaders. (Mem. II. 408; Sh. XVI.)
ELAH, Valley of
(R.V. ELAH, Vale of, ‘or Terebinth’)		 1 Sam. xvii. 2, 19; xxi. 9 Wâdy es Sŭnt 14 The scene of the conflict and death of Goliath. Now called Wâdy es Sŭnt, which passes Shocoh and Gath immediately on the north. (Mem. III.; Sh. XVII.)
ELAM Gen. xiv. 1, 9; Isa. xi. 11; xxi. 2; Jer. xxv. 25; xlix. 34–39; Ezek. xxxii. 24; Dan. viii. 2 The Susiana and Persia of the Greeks.—Grove’s Bible Index.
ELATH, or ELOTH Deut. ii. 8; 1 Kings ix. 26; 2 Kings xiv. 22; xvi. 6; 2 Chr. viii. 17; xxvi. 2 Close to ʾAkabah Ailah — ‘Beside Ezion-geber, on the shore of the Red Sea, in the land of Edom.’ The present town ʾAkabah, or Ailah, at the head of the Gulf of ʾAkabah.
ELEALEH Num. xxxii. 3–37; Isa. xv. 4; xvi. 9; Jer. xlviii. 34 el ʾAl 15 The present ruin ‘el ʾAl,’ near Heshbon.
[p. 56] ELEASA 1 Macc. ix. 5 Kh. Ilʾasa* 14 Now the ruins Ilʾasa, between the Upper and Nether Beth-horon. (Mem. III. 36; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
ELEPH Josh. xviii. 28 Lifta (?)* 14 One of the towns allotted to Benjamin. The present village Lifta (Conder), 2 miles west of Jerusalem.
ELEUTHERUS, The River 1 Macc. xi. 7; xii. 30 Nahr el Kebîr — The modern ‘Nahr el Kebîr,’ north of Tripolis.
ELIM Exod. xv. 27; xvi. 1; Num. xxxiii. 9, 10 Not identified — The second camping station of the Israelites after crossing the Red Sea, and noted for 12 springs and 70 palm-trees. Thought to be ‘Wâdy Ghŭrŭndul,’ on the route from Suez to Jebel Mŭsa.
ELKOSH Nah. i. 1 Not identified — The birth-place of Nahum the prophet. Probably somewhere in Galilee.
ELLASAR Gen. xiv. 1 Senkereh — Now Senkereh, on the left bank of the Euphrates.
ELON Josh. xix. 43 Not identified Perhaps same as Elon-beth-hanan 10 Probably the present village ‘Beit Ello,’ a town on the border of Dan, 8 miles north-west of Bethel (Conder). (Mem. II. 293; Sh. XIV.)
ELON-BETH-HANAN 1 Kings iv. 9 Beit ʾAnân (?)* 14 The present village Beit ʾAnân (Conder), 8½ miles from Jerusalem, on the ancient road leading to Gimzo. (Mem. III. 16; Sh. XVII.)
[p. 57] ELTEKEH
(R.V. ELTEKE Josh. xxi. 23)		 Josh. xix. 44; xxi. 23 Beit Lîkia (?)* 14 One of the cities in the border of Dan. Probably the present Beit Lîkia, 2 miles south of Beth-horon the Nether. (Mem. III. 16; Sh. XVII.)—T. Drake.
ELTEKON Josh. xv. 59 Not identified — One of the towns of Judah, named next to Beth-anoth.
ELTOLAD Josh. xv. 30; xix. 4; 1 Chr. iv. 29 Not identified — One of the cities in the south of Judah, transferred to Simeon = Tolad, 1 Chr. iv. 29.
EMMAUS, Nicopolis 1 Macc. iii. 40, 57; iv. 3; ix. 50; 2 Wars xx. 20, 4; 3, iii. 5; J. Ant. xiii. 1, 3 ʾAmwâs 14 The present village ʾAmwâs, 15 miles from Jerusalem, near the modern road to Jaffa, mentioned by Josephus, 16 Ant. x. 7, 9, etc. (Mem. II. 63; Sh. XVII.)
ENAM Josh. xv. 34 Kh. Wâdy ʾAlîn (?)* 14 Possibly the present ruin ʾAlîn, near Beth-shemesh.—Conder.
ENDOR Josh. xvii. 11; 1 Sam. xxviii. 7; Ps. lxxxiii. 10 Endôr 10 Now the modern village Endôr, 6 miles to the east of Nazareth. (Mem. II. 84; Sh. IX.)
EN-EGLAIM Ezek. xlvii. 10 Not identified — Eusebius places a town of this name 8 miles to the south of ‘Ar Moab’; this would probably mean ‘Kerak.’ ʾAin Hajlah, the ancient Beth Hoglah, has been suggested by Tristram. See Eglaim.
ENGADDI Ecclus. xxiv. 14 ʾAin Jîdy — See En-gedi.
[p. 58] EN-GANNIM (1) Josh. xv. 34 Kh. Umm Jîna 14 A city in the low country of Judah, named between Zanoah and Tappuah. Now the ruin Umm Jîna, west of Beth-shemesh. (Mem. III. 42; Sh. XVII.)—Clermont-Ganneau.
EN-GANNIM (2) Josh. xix. 21; xxi. 29 Jenîn 10 Now the modern town Jenîn, on the extreme south corner of Esdraelon. On or near the border of Issachar. (Mem. II. 44; Sh. VIII.)
EN-GEDI Josh. xv. 62; 1 Sam. xxiii. 29; xxiv. 1; 2 Chr. xx. 2; Cant. i. 14; Ezek. xlvii. 10 ʾAin Jîdy 14 Original name Hazazon-tamar. The well-known spring and ruins of ʾAin Jîdy, on the west shore of the Dead Sea. (Mem. III. 384; Sh. XXII.)
EN-HADDAH Josh. xix. 21 Kefr Adân* 10 On the border of Issachar, and named next to ‘En-gannim.’ Probably the present village Kefr Adân, 3 miles to the west of Jenîn.—Conder. (Mem. II. 45; Sh. VIII.)
EN-HAKKORE Judg. xv. 19 Not identified — The scene of one of Samson’s exploits.
EN-HAZOR Josh. xix. 37 Kh. Hazîreh 6 One of the fenced cities of Naphtali. Now the heap of ruins Hazîreh, on the Naphtali side of the boundary by Wâdy el ʾAyûn. (Mem. I. 204; Sh. IV.)
[p. 59] EN-MISHPAT Gen. xiv. 7 Also called Kadesh. See Kadesh-barnea.
EN-RIMMON Josh. xv. 32; xix. 7; Neh. xi. 29; 1 Chr. iv. 32; Zech. xiv. 10 Kh. Umm er Rŭmâmîn 13 The Ain and Rimmon mentioned together in Josh. xv. 32; xix. 7; 1 Chr. iv. 32, are supposed by some to be one place (?) and identical with the En-rimmon of Neh. xi. 29. The proposed site is that of Kh. Umm er Rŭmâmîn. (Mem. III. 32; Sh. XXIV.)
EN-ROGEL Josh. xv. 7; xviii. 16; 1 Kings i. 9; 2 Sam. xvii. 17 ʾAin Umm ed Dêraj 14 A landmark on the boundary between Judah and Benjamin. The traditional place is ‘Bîr Eyûb’ (a spring well), but the arguments in favour of ‘ʾAin Umm ed Deraj’ (spring of the mother of steps), known to Christians as the ‘Virgin’s Fountain,’ are stronger and more generally accepted.—(Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 334.) See Jerusalem vol., p. 94.
EN-SHEMESH Josh. xv. 7; xviii. 17 ʾAin Haud 14 A landmark on the boundary between Judah and Benjamin, apparently ‘ʾAin Haud,’ east of Bethany (the well of the Apostles—called the Apostles’ fountain by Christians). (Mem. III. 42; Sh. XVII.)
[p. 60] EN-TAPPUAH Josh. xvii. 7 Yasûf (?)* 10 The spring near Yasûf, at the head of the branches of Wâdy Kânah, south of Shechem (Samaritan Chronicle). (Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 263.)
EPHES-DAMMIM 1 Sam. xvii. 1; 1 Chr. xi. 13 Not identified — Or Pas-dammim, ‘the boundary of blood,’ the place where the Philistines encamped before the conflict between David and Goliath took place. Between Socoh and Azekah.
EPHRAIM, EPHRAIN, or EPHRON 2 Sam. xiii. 23; 2 Chron. xiii. 19; John xi. 54 Taiyibeh (?) 10 Named with Bethel and Jeshanah. Apparently Ophrah of Benjamin, which see.
EPHRAIM, Gate of 2 Kings xiv. 13; 2 Chr. xxv. 23; Neh. viii. 16; xii. 39 One of the gates of the city of Jerusalem, probably on the north-west.
EPHRAIM, Mount
(R.V.
EPHRAIM, Hill Country of)		 Josh. xvii. 15; xix. 50; xx. 7; xxi. 21; xxiv. 30, 33; Judg. ii. 9; iii. 27; iv. 5; vii. 24; x. 1; xvii. 1, 8; xviii. 2, 13; xix. 1, 16, 18; 1 Sam. i. 1; ix. 4; xiv. 22; 2 Sam. xx. 21; 1 Kings iv. 8; xii. 25; 2 Kings v. 22; 1 Chr. vi. 67; 2 Chr. xiii. 4; xv. 8; xix. 4; Jer. iv. 15; xxxi. 6; l. 19; Judith vi. 2 The hill country of Ephraim, extending from Bethel and Ramah on the south, to the Great Plain on the north.
[p. 61] EPHRAIM, The Wood of
(R.V.
EPHRAIM, The Forest of)		 2 Sam. xviii. 6 Not identified — Somewhere on the east of Jordan. The forest in which the great battle took place between the forces of Absalom and David. Not far from Mahanaim. (Heth and Moab, p. 180.)
EPHRAIM, Tribe of Josh. xvi.; 5 Ant. i. 22 — ‘The tribe of Ephraim had by lot the land that extended in length from the river Jordan to Gezer; but in breadth as far as from Bethel, till it ended at the Great Plain’ (5 Ant. i. 22).
EPHRATH or EPHRATAH
(R.V.
EPH­RATHAH)		 Gen. xxxv. 16, 19; xlviii. 7; Ruth iv. 11; 1 Chr. ii. 24, 50; Ps. cxxxii. 6; Mic. v. 2 Beit Lahm — The original name of Bethlehem of Judah, which see.
EPHRON 1 Macc. v. 46, 52; 2 Macc. xii. 27 Not identified — One of the strong cities on the east of Jordan, between Ashteroth Karnaim and Beth-shean—was in a valley, and destroyed by Judas Maccabæus.
EPHRON, Mount Josh. xv. 9 — Between the waters of Nephtoah and Kirjath-jearim.
ERECH Gen. x. 10 Warka — One of Nimrod’s cities on the Euphrates, in the neighbourhood of Babylon.
ESDRAELON,
The Great Plain		 Judith i. 8; iii. 9; iv. 6; vii. 3 Merj Ibn ʾAmr 10 This name is the Greek form of the word Jezreel. Now called ‘Merj ibn ʾAmr.’ (Sh. V. and VIII.)
[p. 62] ESEK, The Well Gen. xxvi. 20 Not identified — A well dug by Isaac’s herdmen in the valley of Jerar.
ESHCOL,
Brook or Valley of		 Gen. xiv. 13, 24; Num. xiii. 23, 24; xxxii. 9; Deut. i. 24 Not identified — The name ‘ʾAin Kashkaleh,’ perhaps a remnant of the ancient one, is applied to a spring on the north side of Hebron, near the head of a valley where some of the most extensive vineyards of Palestine exist.
ESHEAN
(R.V. ESHAN)		 Josh. xv. 52 es Sîmia (?)* 14 One of the cities in the mountains of Judah. Possibly the ruin ‘es Sîmia,’ near Dumah. (Mem. III. 313; Sh. XXI.)—Conder.
ESHTAOL Josh. xv. 33; xix. 41; Judg. xiii. 25; xvi. 31; xviii. 2, 8, 11 Eshûʾa 14 Probably the present village Eshûʾa, in the low country of Judah, close to Zorah. (Mem. II. 25; Sh. XVII.)
ESHTEMOA
(R.V. ESHTEMOH, Josh. xv. 50)		 Josh. xv. 50; xxi. 14; 1 Sam. xxx. 28; 1 Chr. iv. 17, 19; vi. 57 es Semûʾa 14 The present village es Semûʾa, in the hill country south of Hebron. (Mem. III. 412, Sh. XXV.)

[p. 63] ETAM (2) 2 Chr. xi. 6; 1 Chr. iv. 3 ʾAin ʾAtân* 14 Probably the village Urtâs, south of Bethlehem, near which is the spring called ʾAin ʾAtân. (Mem. III. 43; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.

ETHAM Exod. xiii. 20; Num. xxxiii. 6 Not identified — One of the stations of the Israelites ‘on the edge of the wilderness.’
ETHER Josh. xv. 42; xix. 7; 1 Chr. iv. 32 Kh. el ʾAtr (?)* 10 Probably the ruin el ʾAtr, near Beit Jibrin, allotted to Simeon. (Mem. III. 261; Sh. XX.)—Conder.
ETHIOPIA Gen. ii. 13; 2 Kings xix. 9; Esth. i. 1; viii. 9; Job xxviii. 19; Ps. lxviii. 31; lxxxvii. 4; Isa. xviii. 1; xx. 3, 5; xxxvii. 9; xliii. 3; xlv. 14; Ezek. xxix. 10; xxx. 4, 5; xxxviii. 5; Nah. iii. 9; Zeph. iii. 10; 1 Esd. iii. 2; Judith i. 10; Esth. xiii. 1; xvi. 1; Acts viii. 27 — Named ‘Cush’ by the Hebrews, and ‘Aithiopia’ by the Greeks. Æthiopia embraced Nubia, Sennaar, Kordofan, and Northern Abyssinia. The name Cush, however, in some cases, if not in all, applies to part of Western Asia south of the Caspian—the country of the Kassi or Cosseans.
EUPHRATES, River Gen. ii. 14; xv. 18; Deut. i. 7; xi. 24; Josh. i. 4; 2 Sam. viii. 3; 2 Kings xxiii. 29;[p. 64] xxiv. 7; 1 Chr. v. 9; xviii. 3; 2 Chr. xxxv. 20; Jer. xiii. 4–7; xlvi. 2, 6, 10; li. 63; 1 Esd. i. 25, 27; 2 Esd. xiii. 43; Judith i. 6; ii. 24; Eccles. xxiv. 26; 1 Macc. iii. 32, 37 —
EZEL, Stone of,
or (R.V., margin, Mound of)		 1 Sam. xx. 19 Not identified — A ‘stone’ or ‘mound,’ the scene of David and Jonathan’s parting.
EZEM 1 Chr. iv. 29 — See Azem.
EZION-GABER or GEBER Num. xxxiii. 35, 36; Deut. ii. 8; 1 Kings ix. 26; xxii. 48; 2 Chr. viii. 17; xx. 36 Not identified — The last camping station of the Israelites before entering the wilderness of Zin, which is Kadesh. ‘King Solomon made a navy of ships in Ezion-geber, which is beside Eloth, on the shore of the Red Sea, in the land of Edom’ (1 Kings ix. 25). In the neighbourhood of ʾAkabah.
GAASH, Mount of
(R.V. Mountain of)		 Josh. xxiv. 30; Judg. ii. 9; 2 Sam. xxiii. 30; 1 Chr. xi. 32 Not identified — In ‘Mount Ephraim,’ near ‘Timnath-serah.’ In Samuel and Chronicles rendered ‘Brooks of Gaash.’

GAD, River of 2 Sam. xxiv. 5 Wâdy Môjib — Same as ‘River Arnon.’

GALAAD Judith i. 8; xv. 5; 1 Macc. v. 9, 17, 20, 25, 27, 36, 45, 55 Gilead — The Greek form of ‘Gilead.’
GALEED Gen. xxxi. 47, 48 — See Jegar-sahadutha.
GALGALA 1 Macc. ix. 2 — Probably Gilgal (2 Kings ii. 1). Now Jiljilia, which see.
GALILEE Josh. xx. 7; xxi. 32; 1 Kings ix. 11; 2 Kings xv. 29; 1 Chr. vi. 76; Isa. ix. 1; 1 Macc. v. 15, 17, 20, 23, 55; x. 30; xi. 63; xii. 47, 49; Tob. i. 2; Judith i. 8; xv. 5; Matt. ii. 22, etc. — The region north of Samaria, including the Plain of Esdraelon and mountains north of it (Cf. 3 Wars, iii. 4).
GALLIM 1 Sam. xxv. 44; Isaiah x. 30 Not identified 14 Possibly ‘Beit Jâla,’ near Bethlehem. (Mem. III. 20; Sh. XVII.)
GAREB, The Hill Jer. xxxi. 39 Not identified — Somewhere in the vicinity of Jerusalem.
GARIZIM 2 Macc. v. 23; vi. 2 Jebel et Tôr — Gerizim.
GATH Josh. xi. 22; 1 Sam. v. 8; vi. 17; vii. 14; xvii. 4, 23, 52; xxi. 10; xxvii. 2, 3, 4, 11; 2 Sam. i. 20; xv. 18; xxi. 20, 22; [p. 66] 1 Kings ii. 39–41; 2 Kings xii. 17; 1 Chr. vii. 21; viii. 13; xviii. 1; xx. 6, 8; 2 Chr. xi. 8; xxvi. 6; Am. vi. 2; Micah i. 10 Tell es Sâfi 13 Five Roman miles from Eleuther­opolis (Beit Jibrîn), on the road to Diospolis (Lydda), according to the Onomasticon. This points to the fortress of ‘Tell es Sâfi.’ (Mem. II. 440; Sh. XVI.)
GATH-HEPHER, or GITTAH-HEPHER Josh. xix. 13; 2 Kings xiv. 25 el Mesh-hed 6 Now the village ‘el Mesh-hed,’ 3 miles north-east of Nazareth, containing the tomb of Jonah (Neby Yûnas). (Mem. I. 365; Sh. VI.)
GATH-RIMMON (1) Josh. xxi. 25 Not identified — A town of Manasseh. In the parallel passage in 1 Chr. vi. 70, the town is called Bileam.
GATH-RIMMON (2) Josh. xix. 45; xxi. 24; 1 Chr. vi. 69 Not identified — Signifying ‘lofty Gath.’ Named between ‘Beneberak’ (Ibn Ibrâk) (Sh. XIII.) and Mejarkon (Nahr el ʾAujeh), north of Jaffa. Probably in the immediate neighbourhood; but no trace has been discovered.
GAZA Gen. x. 19; Josh. x. 41; xi. 22; xv. 47; Jud. i. 18; vi. 4; xvi. 1, 21; 1 Sam. vi. 17; 2 Kings xviii. 8; 1 Chr. vii. 28; Jer. xlvii. 1, 5; Am. i. 6, 7; Zeph. ii. 4; Zech. ix. 5; 1 Macc. xi. 61, 62; xiii. 43; Acts viii. 26 Ghŭzzeh 13 Now the city Ghuzzeh, in Philistia. (Mem. III. 248; Sh. XIX.)
[p. 67] GAZARA 1 Macc. ix. 52; xiii. 53; xiv. 7, 34; xv. 28, 35; xvi. 1, 19, 21; 2 Macc. x. 32 Tell Jezar — Gazera (1 Macc. iv. 15; vii. 35). Tell Jezar. See Gezer.
GEBA (1), GABA or GIBEAH Josh. xxi. 17; 1 Sam. xiii. 3; 2 Sam. v. 25; 1 Kings xv. 22; 2 Kings xxiii. 8; 1 Chr. vi. 60; viii. 6; 2 Chr. xvi. 6; Neh. xi. 31; xii. 29; Isa. x. 29; Zech. xiv. 10 Jebʾa 14 Now the village Jebʾa of Benjamin, near Michmash. (Mem. III. 94; Sh. XVII.)
GEBA (2) Judith iii. 10 Jebʾa 10 Now Jebʾa, a village north of Samaria. (Mem. II. 155, 185; Sh. XI.)
GEBAL Josh. xiii. 5; 1 Kings v. 18; Ps. lxxxiii. 7; Ezek. xxvii. 9 Jebeil — Now the ruined town Jebeil, on the coast, about midway between Beirût and Tripolis.
GEBIM Isa. x. 31 Not identified — North of Jerusalem.
GEDER Joshua xii. 13 Not identified — Named with Debir and Hormah, in the south somewhere, (?) the Gedor of Simeon (1 Chr. iv. 39), or Gedor (1).
GEDERAH, of Judah Josh. xv. 36 Kh. Jedîreh* 14 The Gedor of the Onomasticon, 10 miles from Eleuther­opolis (Beit Jibrin), on the road to Diospolis, now the ruin Jedîreh, 9 miles south of Ludd. (Mem. III. 43; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
[p. 68] GEDERAH, of Benjamin 1 Chr. xii. 4 Jedîreh* 14 The village Jedîreh, north of Jerusalem. (Mem. III. 9; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
GEDEROTH Josh. xv. 41; 2 Chr. xxviii. 18 Katrah (?) 13 Apparently the present village Katrah, also called Cedron (1 Macc. xv. 39). (Mem. III.; Sh. XVI.)—Warren.
GEDERO­THAIM Josh. xv. 36 — According to LXX. was part of Gederah.
GEDOR (1) Josh. xv. 58 Kh. Jedûr 14 The present village Jedûr, in the Hebron mountains, 4 miles north of Hŭlhûl. (Mem. III. 313; Sh. XXI.)
GEDOR (2) 1 Chr. iv. 39 Not identified — Apparently not the same as (1); but somewhere in the south of Judah in Simeon.
GEDOR (3) 1 Chr. xii. 7 Not identified — If belonging to Benjamin, probably Jedîreh. See Gederah of Benjamin.
GEHENNA See Hinnom—Valley of.
GELILOTH Josh. xviii. 17 Not identified — On the south boundary of Benjamin, thought to be a corruption of Gilgal.
GENNESAR, Water of Josh. xiii. Ant. 5, 7; 1 Macc. xi. 67 Bahr Tŭbarîya 6 Now called Bahr Tŭbarîya. See Chinnereth, Sea of.
GEON Eccles. xxiv. 27 — One of the four rivers of Eden, Gihon.

GERIZIM, Mount Deut. xi. 29; xxvii. 12; Josh. viii. 33; Judg. ix. 7 Jebel et Tôr 10 Now called et Tôr, on the south side of the valley, in which Nablus (Shechem) is situated. (Mem. II. 148, 149; Sh. XI.)
GESEM, The Land of Judith i. 9 Goshen — The Greek form of the name Goshen.

GEZER, or GAZER
(R.V. GEZER)		 Josh. x. 33; xii. 12; xvi. 3, 10; xxi. 21; 1 Chr. vi. 67; vii. 28; xx. 4; Judg. i. 29; 1 Kings ix. 15, 16, 17; 2 Sam. v. 25; 1 Chr. xiv. 16; (Gazer) Tell Jezar 13 Now the important site Tell Jezar, 4 miles west of Emmaus (Nicopolis). (Mem. II. 428–432; Sh. XVI.)—Clermont-Ganneau.

[p. 70] GIBEAH, of Judah (1) Josh. xv. 57 Jebʾa* 14 Named with Cain and Timnah. Now the village ‘Jeba,’ 8 miles west of Bethlehem. (Mem. III. 25; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
GIBEAH (2)
(R.V. GIBEATH)		 Josh. xviii. 28 Jebîʾa (?)* 14 A town of Benjamin. Now the ruin Jebîa, between Jerusalem and Emmaus and north of Kirjath. (Mem. III. 43; Sh. XVII.)—Conder.
GIBEAH, of Benjamin or of Saul Judg. xix. 12–16; xx. 4–43; 1 Sam. x. 26; xi. 4; xiii. 2, 15; xiv. 2, 16; xv. 34; xxii. 6; xxiii. 19; xxvi. 1; 2 Sam. xxi. 6; xxiii. 29; 1 Chr. xi. 31; 2 Chr. xiii. 2; Isa. x. 29; Hos. v. 8; ix. 9; x. 9 Not identified — Apparently Gibeah lay somewhere between Geba and Jerusalem. Mentioned as a separate place from Geba in Isa. x. 29. Placed by Robinson at Tell el Fûl, 2½ miles north of Jerusalem. Capt. Conder regards it as a district name.
GIBEAH in the Field Judg. xx. 31 Either Geba (1), or Gibeah.
GIBEAH, of Phinehas Josh. xxiv. 33 ʾAwertah (?)* 10 The burial-place of Eleazar. The traditional site is the village ʾAwertah, south of Shechem (Nâblus), in which are shown the tombs of Eleazar, Phinehas, and Ithamar. Jîbia, 7 miles west of Tell Asûr, has been suggested. (Mem. II. 288; Sh. XIV.)
GIBEAH-HA-ELOHIM 1 Sam. x. 5; xiii. 3 — A garrison of the Philistines = Geba, also a Philistine garrison.—Conder’s Handbook to the Bible.
[p. 71] GIBEON Josh. ix. 3, 17; x. 1–12, 41; xi. 19; xviii. 25; xxi. 17; 2 Sam. ii. 12, 13, 16, 24; iii. 30; xx. 8; 1 Kings iii. 4, 5; ix. 2; 1 Chr. viii. 29; ix. 35; xiv. 16; xvi. 39; xxi. 29; 2 Chr. i. 3, 13; Neh. iii. 7; vii. 25; Is. xxviii. 21; Jer. xxviii. 1; xli. 12, 16 el Jîb — Now the village of ‘el Jîb,’ north of Jerusalem. (Mem. III. 94; Sh. XVII.)
GIDOM Judg. xx. 45 Not identified — Somewhere on the outskirts of Gibeah.
GIHON, River Gen. ii. 13 — The second river of Paradise—Geon.
GIHON 1 Kings i. 33, 38; 45; 2 Chr. xxxii. 30; xxxiii. 14 — = Siloam? The Upper spring of the waters of Gihon (2 Chr. xxxii. 30). ‘ʾAin Umm ed Dêraj,’ ‘the Virgin’s fountain.’ See En Rogel.—Conder’s Handbook to the Bible, p. 335.

‘Gihon, from the fourteenth century, has been supposed to be the Birket Mamilla, and the Lower Gihon to be the Birket es Sultan; but the latter reservoir was only constructed in the twelfth century.’—See Jerusalem vol., p. 94.
GILBOA, Mount 1 Sam. xxviii. 4; xxxi. 1, 8; 2 Sam. i. 6, 21; xxi. 12; 1 Chr. x. 1, 8 Jelbôn 10 The name survives in ‘Jelbôn,’ a village on the high range east of the plain of Esdraelon. (Mem. II. 84; Sh. IX.)
[p. 72] GILEAD, Mount (1) Gen. xxxi. 21, 25; xxxvii. 25; Num. xxxii. 1, 26, 29, 39, 40; iii. 10, 16; iv. Deut. ii. 36; 43; xxxiv. 1; Josh. xii. 2, 5; xiii. 11, 25, 31; xvii. 5, 6; xx. 8; xxi. 38; xxii. 9, 13, 15, 32; Judg. v. 17; x. 4, 8, 17, 18; xi. 5–11, 29; xii. 4–7; xx. 1; Sam. xiii. 7; 2 Sam. ii. 9; xvii. 26; xxiv. 6; 1 Kings iv. 13, 19; xvii. 1; xxii. 3; 2 Kings x. 33; xv. 29; 1 Chr. ii. 22; v. 9, 10, 16; vi. 80; xxvi. 31; xxvii. 21; Ps. lx. 7; cviii. 8; Cant. iv. 1; vi. 5; Jer. viii. 22; xxii. 6; xlvi. 11; l. 19; Ezek. xlvii. 18; Hos. vi. 8; xii. 11; Amos i. 3, 13; Obad. 19; Micah vii. 14; Zech. x. 10 — The mountainous region east of the Jordan; bounded on the north by Bashan, on the east by the Arabian desert, and on the south by Moab and Ammon = The land of Gilead.
GILEAD, Mount (2) Judg. vii. 3 — Probably Gilboa
GILGAL (1) Deut. xi. 30; Josh. iv. 19; v. 9, 10; ix. 6; x. 6, 15, 43; xiv. 6; xv. 7; Judg. ii. 1; iii. 19; 1 Sam. vii. 16; x. 8; xi. 14, 15;[p. 73] xiii. 4–15; xv. 12, 21, 33; 2 Sam. xix. 15, 40; Neh. xii. 29; Hos. iv. 15; ix. 15; xii. 11; Am. iv. 4; v. 5; Micah vi. 5 Jiljûlia 14 Now the ruin Jiljûlia, 3 miles east of Jericho. [p. 74] GOLAN Josh. xx. 8; xxi. 27; Deut. iv. 43; 1 Chr. vi. 71 Sahem el Jaulân (?) 7 One of the three cities of refuge east of the Jordan, in Manasseh. The name has been recovered by G. Schumacher, in the Jaulân. A village exists called Sahem el Jaulân, occupying part of an extensive area of ruins.
GOMORRAH (or Amorah), GOMORRHA (2 Esd. ii. 2) Gen. x. 19; xiii. 10; xiv. 2–11; xviii. 20; xix. 24–28; Deut. xxix. 23; xxxii. 32; Isa. i. 9, 10; xiii. 19; Jer. xxiii. 14; xlix. 18; l. 40; Am. iv. 11; Zeph. ii. 9; Matt. x. 15; Mark vi. 11; Rom. ix. 29; 2 Peter ii. 6; Jude 7 Not identified — At the north end of the Dead Sea there is a valley called ‘Wâdy ʾAmr,’ a word containing the radicals of the name Gomorrah.
GORTYNA 1 Macc. xv. 23 — A city of Crete
GOSHEN (1) GESEM (Judith i. 9) Gen. xlv. 10; xlvi. 28, 29, 34; xlvii. 1, 4, 6, 27; l. 8; Exod. viii. 22; ix. 26 Near the eastern side of the ancient Delta.

(R.V. The ascent of)		 2 Kings ix. 27; Jos. 9 Ant. vi. 4 Not identified — ‘By Ibleam.’ Perhaps Kh. Kâra, west of Yebla.—Conder. See Ibleam.
GUR-BAAL 2 Chr. xxvi. 7 Not identified — A place or district lying between Palestine and the Arabian Peninsula.
HABOR 2 Kings xvii. 6; xviii. 11; 1 Chr. v. 26 Khabour — Called ‘Aborrhas’ by Strabo (XVI. 1, 27); ‘Aburas’ by Isidore of Charax (p. 4); ‘Abora’ by Zosimus (III. 12), and ‘Charboras’ by Pliny and Ptolemy (v. 18). Now called the river Khabour, an affluent of the Euphrates.
HACHILAH, Hill of 1 Sam. xxiii. 19; xxvi. 1, 3 Dhahret el Kolah (?)* 14 Apparently the ridge called ‘el Kolah,’ in the wilderness east of ‘Ziph.’ (Mem. III. 313; Sh. XXI.)—Conder.
HADAD­RIMMON Zech. xii. 11 Rummâneh 10 A place in the valley of Megiddo. Jerome (Comm. in Zach.) makes this = Maximiano­polis, or the present village Rummâneh, west of the plain of ‘Esdraelon.’ (Mem. II. 68; Sh. VIII.)
[p. 76] HADASHAH Josh. xv. 37 Ebdis, ʾEddis* 13 Mentioned between ‘Zenan’ and ‘Migdal-gad.’ Probably the village ‘Ebdis,’ or ‘ʾEddis,’ 6½ miles to the east of Migdal-gad. It is spoken of by Eusebius as lying near Taphna. (Mem. II. 409; Sh. XVI.)
HADATTAH
(R.V. HAZOR-HADATTAH)		 Josh. xv. 25 Not identified — One of the towns of Judah in the south. Should read ‘Hazor-hadattah.’ See Hazor-hadattah.
HADID Ezra ii. 33; Neh. vii. 37; xi. 34 Hadîtheh 10 Named with ‘Lod’ and ‘Ono.’ In the time of Eusebius (Onom. ‘Adithaim’), a town called ‘Aditha,’ or ‘Adatha,’ existed to the east of Lydda (Diospolis). ‘Adida in Sephela’ (1 Macc. xii. 38) is probably the same place. Now the present village ‘Hadîtheh,’ 3 miles to the east of Lydda = the Adithaim of Joshua xv. 36. (Mem. II. 322; Sh. XIV.)
HADRACH, The land of Zech. ix. 1 Not identified — Somewhere in Syria.
HAI
(R.V. AI)		 Gen. xii. 8; xiii. 3 — See ‘Ai.’
HALAH 2 Kings xviii. 11; 1 Chr. v. 26 Not identified — A different place to that of Gen. x. 11; thought to be the ‘Chalcitis’ of Ptolemy (v. 18). The modern name, ‘Gla,’ applies to a huge mound on the Upper Khabour, above its junction with the Jerujer. (Layard, Nin. & Bab. 312.)
[p. 77] HALAK, Mount Josh. xi. 17; xii. 7 Not identified — In the neighbourhood of ‘Mount Seir,’ signifying ‘the bare mountain’ (margin R.V.).
HALHUL Josh. xv. 58 Hŭlhûl 14 The present village still called ‘Hŭlhûl,’ north of Hebron and near to Beth-zur, with which it is named. (Mem. III. 305; Sh. XXI.)
HALI Josh. xix. 25 Kh. ʾAlia (?)* 6 A town on the boundary of Asher, named between ‘Helkath’ and ‘Beten.’ The name Kh. ʾAlia, some 13 miles south-east of Akka is suggestive of this site, and may probably be in the district of ‘Aloth,’ which see. (Mem. I. 170; Sh. III.)
HALICAR­NASSUS 1 Macc. xv. 23; Jo. Ant. xiv. 10, 23 Budrûm — A city in ‘Caria,’ celebrated for its harbour and the strength of its fortifi­cations, the birth-place of Herodotus and of the later historian, Dionysius. A plan of the site is given in Ross, Reisen auf den Griech Inseln (vol. iv., p. 30). The modern name is ‘Budrûm.’
HAM Gen. xiv. 5 Not identified — Thought to be another form of Ammon. The Targums of Onkelos and Pseudo Jonathan have Hemta. Schwartz (217) suggests ‘Humeitat,’ or ‘Hammet Animah,’ 1 mile north of ‘Rabba.’
[p. 78] HAMATH Num. xiii. 21; xxxiv. 8; Josh. xiii. 5; Judg. iii. 3; 2 Sam. viii. 9; 1 Kings viii. 65; 2 Kings xiv. 25, 28; xvii. 24, 30; xviii. 34; xix. 13; xxiii. 33; xxv. 21; 1 Chr. xiii. 5; xviii. 3, 9; 2 Chr. vii. 8; viii. 4; Isa. x. 9; xi. 11; xxxvi. 19; xxxvii. 13; Jer. xxxix. 5; xlix. 23; lii. 9, 27; Ezek. xlvii. 16, 17, 20; xlviii. 1; Amos vi. 2, 14; Zech. ix. 2 Hama — The present city Hama, in the valley of the Orontes, north of Damascus. Hemath (Amos vi. 14).
HAMATH ZOBAH 2 Chr. viii. 3 Not identified — Perhaps same as last. North of Damascus.
HAMMATH Josh. xix. 35 Hŭmmâm Ibrahim Basha 6 One of the fortified cities of Naphtali. The site was probably at the Emmaus of Josephus, so famed for its hot springs and baths (xviii. Ant. 2, 3; 4 Wars i. 3). Now Hammâm Tabariya. (Mem. I. 379; Sh. VI.)
HAMMON Josh. xix. 28 ʾAin Hamûl 6 The present ruin Hima, 11 miles south-east of Tyre, ‘Kh. Umm el ʾAmud,’ on the coast 10 miles south of Tyre, and ‘ʾAin Hamûl’ (Schwartz), a little farther south, have each been proposed. (Mem. I. 51 & 176; Sh. III., and Conder’s Handbook to the Bible.)
[p. 79] HAMMON 1 Chr. vi. 76 — Allotted out of the tribe of Naphtali to the Levites. Possibly the same as Hammath.
HAMMOTH-DOR Josh. xxi. 32 — Same as Hammon (1 Chr. vi. 76), and Hammath of Josh. xix. 35.

(R.V. HANANEL)		 Neh. iii. 1; xii. 39; Jer. xxxi. 38; Zech. xiv. 10 Not identified — A tower which formed part of the wall of Jerusalem, between the Sheepgate and the Fishgate.
HANES Isa. xxx. 4 Tell Defenneh — A place in Egypt, (?) Tahpanes, which see.

(R.V.
HAPHARA-IM)		 Josh. xix. 19 Kh. Farrîyeh* 10 Probably the present ruin Farrîyeh, west of the plain of Esdraelon. The site of Affarea, 6 miles north of Legio—‘Lejjun.’ Onomasticon, s.v. Haphraim. A city of Issachar. (Mem. II. 58; Sh. VIII.)—Conder.

HARETH, The Forest of
(R.V. HERETH)		 1 Sam. xxii. 5; Ant. vi. 12, 4 Kharâs (?)* 14 The LXX. reads ‘city.’ Very probably the name is preserved in that of Kharâs, a village in the Hebron mountains, between ‘Hŭlhul’ and ‘Adullam,’ where dense patches of scrub abound. Mem. III. 305; Sh. XXI.—Conder.
HAROD, The Well of Judg. vii. 1 ʾAin Jalûd (?) 10 ʾAin Jalûd, below Jezreel (Zerʾîn), is the generally-accepted spring. Capt. Conder suggests ‘ʾAin el Jemʾâin (the spring of two troops), near Beth-shean. (Mem. II. 79, 81; Sh. IX.)
HAROSHETH of the Gentiles Judg. iv. 2, 13, 16 el Harathîyeh (?) 6 The village ‘el Harathiyeh,’ in the narrow strait, on the north bank of the River Kishon, which separates Lower Galilee from Carmel, is generally looked to now as the ancient site; whilst others maintain that it was situated in the Upper Jordan Valley, near the Lake Huleh—Merom. (Mem. I. 270; Sh. V.)
HARUPH, HARIPH 1 Chr. xii. 5; Neh. vii. 24 Kh. Kharûf (?)* — Appears to have been in the south of Judah. Probably Kh. Kharûf, south of ʾAid el Mâ. (Mem. III. 313; Sh. XXI.)—Conder.
[p. 81] HASHMONAH Num. xxxiii. 29, 30 Not identified — One of the camping stations of the Israelites, somewhere near ‘Mount Hôr.’
HAURAN Ezek. xlvii. 16, 18 Hauran 7 A province of Palestine, bounded on the west by Gaulanitis, on the north by the wild and rocky district of Trachonitis, on the east by the mountainous region of Batanæa, and on the south by the great plain of Moab. (See Porter’s Damascus, vol. ii.)
HAVILAH Gen. ii. 11; x. 7, 29; xxv. 18; 1 Sam. xv. 7; 1 Chr. i. 9, 23 Not identified —
HAVOTH-JAIR Num. xxxii. 41; Deut. iii. 14; Josh. xiii. 30; 1 Chr. ii. 23; 1 Kings iv. 13 Not identified — ‘Small towns of Jair,’ in the country of Argob.
HAZAR-ADDAR Num. xxxiv. 4 Not identified — = Addar. On the southern boundary of Judah, between Kadesh Barnea and Azmon.
HAZAR-ENAN Num. xxxiv. 9, 10; Ezek. xlvii. 17; xlviii. i. 1 Not identified — The northern limit of the Promised Land. ‘Kuryetein,’ a village north-east of Damascus some 60 miles, has been proposed by Porter. (Damascus i. 252; ii. 358.) Conder suggests ʾAin el ʾAsi (see Heth & Moab).
HAZAR-GADDAH Josh. xv. 27 Not identified — One of the towns in the south of Judah, named between ‘Moladah’ and ‘Heshmon.’
[p. 82] HAZAR-HATTICON
(R.V. HAZER-HATTICON)		 Ezek. xlvii. 16 Not identified — On the boundary of Hauran. Said to mean ‘middle village’ (R.V.)
HAZAR-SHUAL Josh. xv. 28; xix. 3; 1 Chr. iv. 28; Neh. xi. 27 Not identified — One of the towns in the south of Judah, named next to Beer-sheba.
HAZAR-SUSAH Josh. xix. 5; 1 Chr. iv. 31 Susîn (?) — One of the southern cities of Judah allotted to Simeon. Or ‘Hazar-susim,’ ‘the village of horses.’ Probably the ruin Susîn, on the caravan road to Egypt, some 10 miles south of Gaza.—Tristram.
HAZAR­MAVETH Gen. x. 26; 1 Chr. i. 20 Hadramâut — Now Hadramaut, a district in south-east of Arabia.
HAZERIM Deut. ii. 23 — ‘The villages’ of the Avims.
HAZEROTH Num. xi. 35; xii. 16; xxxiii. 17; Deut. i. 1 ʾAin Hudherah (?) — The next camping station of the Israelites after ‘Kibroth-hattaavah.’ ‘Ain Hudherah,’ some two or three days’ journey north-east from Sinai, was first suggested by Burckhardt.—Burckhardt, p. 495; Robinson, vol. i., p. 223.
HAZEZON-TAMAR
(R.V.
HAZAZON-TAMAR)		 Gen. xiv. 7; 2 Chron. xx. 2 ʾAin Jidy 14 The original name of En-gedi (2 Chr. xx. 2). The name is probably preserved in that of the tract called ‘Hasâseh’ (pebbles), near ‘ʾAin Jîdy.’ Compare Ziz, cliff of.
[p. 83] HAZOR (1) Josh. xi. 1, 10–13; xii. 19; xix. 36; Jud. iv. 2, 17; 1 Sam. xii. 9; 1 Kings ix. 15; 2 Kings xv. 29; Jer. xlix. 28, 30, 33 Jebel Hadîreh (?) 6 Named between ‘Ramah’ and ‘Kedesh’ (Kades) as one of the fenced cities of Naphtali. The name survives in Jebel Hadîreh, near Kades in Upper Galilee. (Mem. I. 204; Sh. IV.)
HAZOR (2) Josh. xv. 23 Not identified — One of the uttermost cities of Judah in the south; also called Kerioth Hezron in Josh. xv. 25.
HAZOR-HADATTAH (3) Josh. xv. 25 Not identified — One of the towns of Judah in the south; should read ‘Hazor-hadattah’ (R.V.), and this reading is given by Eusebius and Jerome, who speak (Onom. ‘Asor’) of ‘New Hazor’ as being situated to the east of and near Ascalon.
HAZOR (4) Neh. xi. 33; 1 Kings ix. 15 Kh. Hazzûr 14 Now the heap of ruins ‘Hazzûr,’ north of Jerusalem, near Beit Hanîna, and in Benjamin. (Mem. III. 43; Sh. XVII.)
HEBRON Gen. xiii. 18; xxiii. 2, 19; xxxv. 27; xxxvii. 14; Num. xiii. 22; Jos. x. 3, 5, 23, 36, 39; xi. 21; xii. 10; xiv. 54; xx. 7; xxi. 13–15; xv. 13, 11, 13; Judg. i. 10, 20; xvi. 3; 1 Sam. xxx. 31; 2 Sam. ii. 1, 3, 11, 32; iii. 2, 32; iv. 1–12;[p. 84] v. 1–13; xv. 7–10; 1 Kings ii. 11; 1 Chr. ii. 42, 43; iii. 1, 4; vi. 2, 55, 57; xi. 1, 3; xii. 23, 38; xxix. 27; 2 Chr. xi. 10; 1 Macc. v. 65 el Khŭlîl 14 One of the oldest cities of Palestine, built seven years before ‘Zoan’ in Egypt (Num. xiii. 22). Originally named Kirjath-arba (Judg. i. 10). The burial-place of Abraham, Sarah, Isaac, and Jacob. One of the six cities of refuge. Now a large town called ‘el Khulîl.’ (Mem. III. 305; Sh. XXI.)
HEBRON
(R.V. EBRON)		 Josh. xix. 28 — See ‘Abdon,’ a town of Asher, which is thought to represent this place.
HELAM 2 Sam. x. 16, 17 Not identified — Between the Jordan and Euphrates, thought to be identical with Alamatha, a town named by Ptolemy, on the west of the Euphrates, near Nicephorium.
HELBAH Judg. i. 31 Not identified 6 A town in Asher.
HELBON Ezek. xxvii. 18 Helbôn 3 Now represented by the village still called Helbôn, in the mountains, 13 miles north of Damascus. (Five years in Damascus, II. 330.—Porter.)
HELEPH Josh. xix. 33 Beit Lîf 6 On the boundary of Naphtali. Van de Velde proposed Beit Lîf. (Mem. I. 204; Sh. IV.)
HELKATH Josh. xix. 25; xxi. 31 Yerka (?) 6 Mentioned next to ‘Hali’ (Kh. ʾAlia) in Josh. xix. 25, and to ‘Rehob’ in xxi. 31. On the boundary of Asher. The village ‘Yerka,’ 8½ miles to east of ʾAkka, proposed by Van de Velde. In 1 Chr. vi. 75, it is rendered ‘Hukok.’
[p. 85] HELKATH-HAZZURIM 2 Sam. ii. 16 Wâdy el ʾAskar (?)* 14 Possibly ‘Wâdy el ʾAskar,’ between ‘Gederah’ (Jedîreh) and ‘Gibeon’ (el Jîb). (Mem. III.; Sh. XVII.)—C. F. T. Drake.
HEMATH Amos vi. 14 Hama — = Hamath.
HENA 2 Kings xviii. 34; 2 Kings xix. 13; Is. xxxvii. 13 ʾAnah (?) — Probably ‘Anah,’ near ‘Mosaib,’ on the Euphrates.
HEPHER Josh. xii. 17; 1 Kings iv. 10 Not identified — Named between ‘Tappuah’ and Aphek in Josh. xii. 17, and between Socoh (Shuweikeh), and Dôr (Tanturah), 1 Kings iv. 10. Not Gath Hepher.
HERES, Mount Judg. i. 35 — Mentioned with Aijalon. Some 5 miles to the north of the valley of Aijalon is the village of ‘Khŭrbetha ibn Hârith,’ 5 miles due east of this place is a very prominent and commanding hill top called ‘Batn Harâsheh.’ Further north lie Hâris and Kefr Hâris (Timnath Heres). All these names may be connected with that of Mount Heres.
HERMON, Mount Deut. iii. 8, 9; iv. 48; Josh. xi. 3, 17; xii. 1–5; xiii. 5, 11; 1 Chr. v. 23; Ps. xlii. 6; lxxxix. 12; cxxxiii. 3; Song. iv. 8; Eccles. xxiv. 13 Jebel esh Sheikh
Jebel eth Thelj		 — Now called ‘Jebel esh Sheikh,’ or ‘Jebel eth Thelj,’ the highest mountain in the Anti-Lebanon range (9,166 feet). Special Papers Vol., p. 115–116.
[p. 86] HESHBON Num. xxi. 25–34; xxxii. 3, 37; Deut. i. 4; ii. 24, 30; iii. 2, 6; iv. 46; xxix. 7; Josh. ix. 10; xii. 2, 5; xiii. 10, 17, 21, 26, 27; xxi. 39; Judg. xi. 19, 26; 1 Chr. vi. 81; Neh. ix. 22; Cant. vii. 4; Is. xv. 4; xvi. 8, 9; Jer. xlviii. 2, 34, 45; xlix. 3 Hesbân 15 The capital of Sihon King of the Amorites, rebuilt by the children of Reuben (Num. xxxii. 37). Near or on the border between Reuben and Dan. In Joshua xiii. 17, as belonging to Reuben, and in Joshua xxi. 39 and 1 Chr. vi. 81, mentioned as given ‘out of the tribe of Gad.’ Now the ruined city ‘Hesbân.’ For details see Quarterly Statement, 1882, p. 8, Eastern Survey.
HESHMON Josh. xv. 27 Not identified — Named with ‘Beer-sheba,’ ‘Moladah,’ etc. Apparently to the south; thought to be another form of the name ‘Azmon,’ which see.
HETHLON Ezek. xlvii. 15; xlviii. 1 — Supposed to be the Pass at the northern end of Mount Lebanon, from the Mediterranean to the great Plain of Hamath—and would thus be identical with ‘the entrance to Hamath.’ (Five Years in Damascus II. 356.)—Porter.
HEZRON Josh. xv. 3 J. Hadîreh (?)* 20 Named as being on the southern boundary of Judah and between ‘Kadesh-barnea’ and ‘Adar.’ ‘Jebel Hadîreh,’ south of Bîr-sheba, proposed by Capt. Conder. (See Handbook to the Bible, p. 257.) The position agrees, and the Arabic name is radically the same as the Hebrew.
[p. 87] HIDDEKEL Gen. ii. 14; Dan. x. 14 River Tigris — One of the rivers of Eden, ‘which goeth toward the east of Assyria.’ The old name of the Tigris, which is now called Dijlah.
HILEN 1 Chron. vi. 58 Not identified — In Joshua xv. 51, = Holon, which see.
HINNOM, Valley of Josh. xv. 8; xviii. 16; 2 Kings xxiii. 10; 2 Chr. xxviii. 3; xxxiii. 6; Neh. xi. 30; Jer. vii. 31, 32; xix. 2, 6; xxxii. 35 Wâdy er Rabâbeh (?) 14 Now ‘Wâdy er Rabâbeh’—the valley surrounding Jerusalem on the west and south.—Jerusalem Vol. p. 94. Some have thought the Kedron Valley to be intended.
HOBAH Gen. xiv. 15 Jôbar (?) or Buzreh (?) 3 The Jews of Damascus have a tradition that the village of ‘Jôbar,’ immediately north of Damascus, is the ‘Hobah’ of Scripture. Again, the Moslems have another tradition that Abraham took refuge in a cleft of the rock in Buzreh, which is farther north and to the west of Jobâr.—Porter’s Handbook for Syria and Palestine, pp. 491, 492. The Hebrew word is said to mean ‘hiding.’
HOLON (1), or HILEN Josh. xv. 51; xxi. 15; 1 Chron. vi. 58 Beit ʾAlâm (?)* 14 A town in the mountains of Judah, named between ‘Goshen’ (not recovered) and Giloh (Kh. Jala.) In the same group as ‘Dannah’ (Idhna)—very probably the ruins ‘Beit ʾAlâm’ (Sheet 14.) (Mem. III. 313; Sh. XXI.)—Conder.
[p. 88] HOLON (2) Jer. xlviii. 21 Not identified — In the ‘plain country,’ or Mishor in Moab. Perhaps ‘ʾAleiyan.’—Conder.
HOR, Mount (1) Numb. xxxiv. 7, 8 Not identified — One of the landmarks on the northern limits of the boundary of the Promised Land. Supposed to be the Lebanon Range. (See Conder’s Heth & Moab.)
HOR, Mount (2) Num. xx. 22–27; xxi. 4; xxxiii. 37, 41; Deut. xxxii. 50 Jebel Neby Harûn 28 The next camping station of the Israelites after ‘Kadesh’ (Num. xx. 22); ‘By the coast of the land of Edom’ (Num. xx. 23); or ‘in the edge’ (xxxiii. 37.) ‘And Aaron went up into “Mount Hor” and died there’ (Num. xxxiii. 38.) A double-peaked mountain on the eastern side of the ‘Wâdy ʾArabah,’ and about midway between ‘the Salt Sea’ and the Gulf of ʾAkabah. The northern peak is the highest one, on which is the traditional tomb of Aaron. A great open plain extends from the western base into the ‘Wâdy ʾArabah’—and has an area of about 20 square miles. At a higher elevation of 1,000 feet above this plain and between the eastern base of the mountain and Petra, is the open piece of rolling land—called ‘the Plain of Aaron,’ which is encircled by the surrounding peaks[p. 89] and over 2 square miles in extent. There is also a little plateau at the fork of the two peaks (now called Jebel Neby Harûn.)—For various descriptions see the records of Burckhardt, Irby and Mangles, Stephens, Wilson, Robinson, Martineau, Stanley. (Professor Hull’s Mt. Seir, also the Quarterly Statement, October, 1884.)—Major Kitchener.
HOREB, Mount Exod. iii. 1; xvii. 6; xxxiii. 6; Deut. i. 2, 6, 19; iv. 10, 15; v. 2; ix. 8; xviii. 16; xxix. 1; 1 Kings viii. 9; xix. 8; 2 Chr. v. 10; Ps. cvi. 19; Mal. iv. 4; Eccles. xlviii. 7 Not identified — ‘The Mount of God’—another name for Sinai and the wilderness. ‘The rock in Horeb’ = Massah and Meribah. Exodus xvii. 7. The name in Hebrew means ‘desert’ or ‘dry,’ and may apply to the whole Sinaitic block.
HOREM Josh. xix. 38 Kh. Hârah* 6 Named between Migdal-el (Mujeidel) and Beth-anath (Ainitha) in Naphtali. Now the ruin Hârah, between these two places. (Mem. I. 205; Sh. IV.)—Conder.
HOR-HAGIDGAD
(R.V. HOR-HAGGIDGAD)		 Num. xxxiii. 32, 33 Not identified — One of the camping stations of the Israelites in the desert.
HORMAH or ZEPHATH Num. xiv. 45; xxi. 3; Deut. i. 44; Josh. xii. 14; xv. 30; xix. 4; Judg. 1, 17; 1 Sam. xxx. 30; 1 Chron. iv. 30 Not identified — Also called ‘Zephath’ (Judg. i. 17.) Named between Geder (not recovered) and Arad (Tell ʾArâd)[p. 90] Josh. xii. 14. Also between Chesil or Bethul (Beit Âûla) Sheet 14, and Ziklag: xv. 30; xix. 4. Robinson (II. 181) identifies the pass es Sŭfa with Zephath (Sheet 21.) S’baita, south of Beersheba (Sheet 20) is also proposed and has many supporters. The name Kh. Hôra (Sheet 13) east of Beersheba, exists at a very ancient site. (Mem. III. 396; Sh. XXIV.) S’beita does not represent the Hebrew, which is correctly rendered by Sŭfa, as Robinson proposes.
HORONAIM Is. xv. 5; Jer. xlviii. 3, 5, 34 Not identified — Possibly ‘Wâdy Ghûeir’ (with ancient road). The Hebrew and Arabic have the same meaning, with a slight change of guttural. (Conder, Heth and Moab, 403) situated between ‘Beth Jesimoth’ (Sheet 14) and ‘Luhith’ (Sheet 15.)
HOSAH Josh. xix. 29 ʾEzzîyat el Fôka or et Tahta (?)* 6 A city of Asher. Probably the present ruins now called ‘ʾEzzîyat el Fôka,’ south of Tyre. (Mem. I. 48, 51; Sh. I.)—Conder.
HUKKOK Josh. xix. 34 Yakûk 6 Named next to ‘Aznoth Tabor’ as being on the boundary of Naphtali. The present village Yakûk. (Mem. I. 365; Sh. VI.)
[p. 91] HUKOK 1 Chr. vi. 75 Not identified — Apparently another name for ‘Helkath’ of Joshua xix. 25
HUMTAH Josh. xv. 54 Not identified — In the mountains of Judah, and mentioned next to Hebron.
HYDASPES, River Judith i. 6 Not identified — Possibly the Choaspes of Susiana. Not the Hydaspes of India (Smith’s Bible Dictionary.)
IBLEAM Josh. xvii. 11; Judg. i. 27; 2 Kings ix. 27 Yebla 6 A city of Manasseh in Issachar. Probably Yebla, north-west of Beth-shean. See also Bileam.
IDALAH Josh. xix. 15 el Huwarah (?)* 6 One of the cities of Zebulon. Its later name was Hirii (Talmud Jer, Megillah I.) Now identified with ‘el Huwarah,’ south of Bethlehem in Zebulon. (See Conder’s Handbook, p. 268, and Mem. I. 288; Sh. V.)
IDUMEA
(R.V. EDOM)		 Is. xxxiv. 5, 6; Ezek. xxxv. 15; xxxvi. 5; 1 Macc. iv. 15, 29, 61; v. 3; vi. 31; 2 Macc. xii. 32; Mark iii. 8 See Edom — The Greek form of the name Edom.

(R.V. IYIM)		 Num. xxxiii. 45 See Ije-abarim — A contracted form of the name Ije-abarim, which see.
IIM (2) Josh. xv. 29 Not identified — Mentioned with ‘Beer-sheba,’ and ‘Chesil,’ or ‘Bethul,’ somewhere in the south of Judah. The Peshito Syriac version has Elin.

(R.V. IYE-ABARIM)		 Num. xxi. 11; xxxiii. 44 Not identified — Between ‘Oboth’ and ‘the valley of Zared,’ ‘wilderness which is before Moab.’ One of the camping stations of the Israelites.
IJON 1 Kings xv. 20; 2 Kings xv. 29; 2 Chr. xvi. 4 el Khîam (?)* 6 A town belonging to the tribe of Naphtali, ‘el Khîam,’ in the Merj ʾAyûn, north of Banias (Conder). Tell Dibbin, in the same district, has also been proposed. (Mem. I. 88; Sh. II.)
IMMER Ezra ii. 59; Neh. vii. 61 Not identified — One of the places from which some of the captivity returned, who could not prove their pedigree.

[p. 93] ISSACHAR, Tribe of Gen. xxx. 18; xxxv. 23; xlvi. 13; xlix. 14; Exod. i. 3; Num. i. 8, 28, 29; ii. 5; vii. 18; x. 15; xiii. 7; xxvi. 23, 25; xxxiv. 26; Deut. xxvii. 12; xxxiii. 18; Josh. xvii. 10, 11; xix. 17, 23; xxi. 6, 28; Judg. v. 15; x. 1; 1 Kings iv. 17; xv. 27; 1 Chron. ii. 1; vi. 62, 72; vii. 1, 5; xii. 32, 40; xxvii. 18; 2 Chr. xxx. 18; Ezek. xlviii. 25, 26–33; Rev. vii. 7 — ‘The fourth lot came out for Issachar. And their border was unto Jezreel, and Chesulloth and Shunem; and Haphraim, and Shion, and Anaharath; and Rabbith, and Kishion, and Ebez; and Remeth, and En-gannim, and En-haddah, and Beth-pazzez; and the border reached to Tabor, and Shahazumah, and Beth-shemesh; and the goings out of their border were at Jordan; sixteen cities with their villages.’ (Josh. xix. 17–23 R.V.) ‘Issachar had its limits in length, Mount Carmel and the river, but its limit in breadth was Mount Tabor.’ (5 Ant. JAAZER

[p. 94] JABBOK, River Gen. xxxii. 22; Num. xxi. 24; Deut. ii. 37; iii. 16; Josh. xii. 2; Judg. xi. 13–22 Wâdy Zêrka 11 The brook which Jacob crossed on his way from ‘Haran.’ Between Gerasa (Jerash) and Philadelphia (Amman)—Onomasticon. Now called Wâdy ez Zêrka, having its source at the clear and copious springs in the valley above ‘Ammân,’ then sweeping round in a north-westerly direction to the south of Jerash, and entering the Jordan near ‘Succoth’ and ‘Adam.’
JABESH-GILEAD Judg. xxi. 8, 14; 1 Sam. xi. 1–10; xxxi. 11–13; 2 Sam. ii. 4, 5; xxi. 12; 1 Chr. x. 11, 12 Not identified 11 Six Roman miles from Pella on the road to Gerasa (Onomasticon.) The name survives in Wâdy el Yâbis, and possibly the ruin ed Deir marks the site.
JABEZ 1 Chron. ii. 55 Not identified — ‘Deir Abu Kabûs, between Eshtaol and Ashnah, has been proposed for this place.’ (Henderson’s Handbook to Students.) The Arabic and Hebrew have, however, no connection.
JABNEEL, or JABNEH Josh. xv. 11; 2 Chron. xxvi. 6; 1 Macc. iv. 15; v. 58; x. 69; xv. 40; 2 Macc. xii. 8, 9, 40 Yebnah 13 One of the places on the northern boundary of Judah. Now the village Yebnah, in Philistia. The Jamnia of the 1st Book of Maccabees. (Mem. II. 441; Sh. XVI.)
